**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Biological Entity                      Associated Characteristic
1. B cells                               : Originates in the thymus
2. T cells                               :  Mediates humoral immunity
3. Plasma cells                           : Differentiates from memory B cells
4. Helper T cells (Th)                   : Activates cytotoxic T cells
5. Memory B cells                         : Produces antibodies


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 4 and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Option (d) is correct because Helper T cells (Th) do activate cytotoxic T cells, and memory B cells are indeed a type of B cell that provides long-term immunity without directly producing antibodies.  The other options contain inaccuracies. B cells originate in the bone marrow, not the thymus (incorrect in pair 1). T cells mediate cellular immunity, not humoral immunity (incorrect in pair 2). Plasma cells differentiate directly from activated B cells, not memory B cells (incorrect in pair 3).


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Organism Type                          Symbiotic Relationship Example
1. Fungi                                 :  Mycorrhizal association with algae
2. Cnidarians                            :  Mutualistic relationship with clownfish
3. Protozoa                              :  Endosymbiotic relationship with termites
4. Bacteria                              :  Nitrogen fixation in legume roots
5. Lichens                               : Symbiotic relationship between fungus and algae


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All five pairs represent accurate examples of symbiotic relationships. Fungi participate in mycorrhizal associations with plant roots (and algae in the case of lichens). Cnidarians (like sea anemones) have a mutualistic relationship with clownfish. Protozoa have endosymbiotic relationships with various organisms, including termites. Bacteria are crucial for nitrogen fixation in legume root nodules. Lichens are a classic example of a symbiotic relationship between a fungus and an alga.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Biological Entity                      Culturing Method
1. Bacteria                              :  Artificial media
2. Fungi                                 :  Synthetic agar plates
3. Viruses                               :  Cell cultures
4. Algae                                 :  Liquid media
5. Protozoa                              :  Liquid media


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 1, 2, and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All listed organisms can be cultured in the specified media. Bacteria and fungi are routinely grown on various artificial and synthetic media. Viruses, being obligate intracellular parasites, require cell cultures for propagation. Algae and protozoa are often cultured in liquid media.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Organism                                 Habitat
1. Fern                                   :  Soil-less environment
2. Lichen                                  :  Rocky surfaces
3. Moss                                   :  Surface without soil
4. Mushroom                              :  Moist environments
5. Algae                                  :  Aquatic and soil environments


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 2, 3, 4, and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Lichens are well-known for their ability to thrive on rocky surfaces and other substrates lacking soil. Mosses also frequently colonize surfaces without soil. Mushrooms typically require moist environments for growth.  Ferns usually require soil for growth. Algae can inhabit various environments but are not exclusively found in soil-less habitats.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Factor                                  Effect on Pressure Cooker Cooking Temperature
1. Area of the hole in the lid           :  Directly influences the pressure
2. Temperature of the flame             :  Affects the rate of heating
3. Weight of the lid                      :  Determines the pressure inside the cooker


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The weight of the lid directly impacts the pressure inside the cooker, which, in turn, affects the boiling point of water and thus the cooking temperature. The area of the hole influences pressure release and thus indirectly affects the temperature. The flame temperature affects the rate of heating but not directly the cooking temperature once the pressure is established.


**6. Consider the following pairs:**

   Product                                 Characteristic
1. Furnace oil                            :  By-product of petroleum refining
2.  Sulphur dioxide                       :  Air pollutant from copper smelting
3. Carbon monoxide                       :  Greenhouse gas
4.  Heavy metals                         :  Can leach from copper slag
5.  Triethylaluminum and Triethylboron    :  Components of rocket engine igniters


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Furnace oil is indeed a by-product of petroleum refining. Copper smelting releases sulfur dioxide as a pollutant, and heavy metals can leach from copper slag. Triethylaluminum and triethylboron are used in certain rocket engine igniters. Carbon monoxide is a toxic gas but not primarily considered a greenhouse gas in the same way as carbon dioxide.  Therefore, only pairs 1, 2, 4, and 5 are correctly matched.


**7. Consider the following pairs:**

   Immune Cell Type                       Function
1. B cells                                :  Produce antibodies
2. T cells                                :  Directly kill infected cells
3. Plasma cells                           :  Present antigens to T cells
4. Helper T cells (Th)                   :  Activate B cells and other T cells
5. Macrophages                            :  Phagocytose pathogens


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 4, and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

B cells produce antibodies, a key component of humoral immunity.  Cytotoxic T cells directly kill infected cells. Helper T cells activate both B cells and other T cells. Macrophages are phagocytic cells that engulf and destroy pathogens.  Plasma cells are not antigen-presenting cells; that role belongs to macrophages, dendritic cells, and B cells. Therefore, only pairs 1, 2, 4, and 5 are correctly matched.


**8. Consider the following pairs:**

   Vaccine Type                            Mechanism of Action
1. mRNA Vaccine                           :  Introduces viral mRNA to produce an immune response
2.  Live attenuated vaccine               :  Uses weakened pathogens to stimulate immunity
3.  Inactivated vaccine                   :  Uses killed pathogens to elicit an immune response
4.  Subunit vaccine                       :  Uses specific viral proteins to trigger immunity
5.  Conjugate vaccine                     :  Combines a weak antigen with a stronger one to enhance response


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 1, 2, and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All five pairs accurately describe the mechanisms of action of the respective vaccine types.  mRNA vaccines introduce mRNA to produce a viral protein, triggering an immune response. Live-attenuated vaccines use weakened versions of the pathogen. Inactivated vaccines use killed pathogens. Subunit vaccines use only specific parts of the pathogen. Conjugate vaccines combine a weak antigen with a stronger one to boost the immune response.


**9. Consider the following pairs:**

   Immune System Component                 Role in Immunity
1. Antibodies                             :  Neutralize pathogens
2. Antigens                               :  Trigger immune responses
3. B cells                                :  Mediate humoral immunity
4. T cells                                :  Mediate cellular immunity
5. Cytokines                              :  Regulate immune responses


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 1, 2, and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All five pairs correctly match the immune system component with its role. Antibodies neutralize pathogens by binding to them. Antigens are substances that trigger an immune response. B cells mediate humoral immunity. T cells mediate cellular immunity. Cytokines are signaling molecules that regulate various aspects of immune responses.



**10. Consider the following pairs:**

    Medical Technology                       Application
1. CAR T-cell therapy                     :  Treats certain types of leukemia
2.  Mitochondrial Replacement Therapy (MRT): Prevents mitochondrial diseases from being passed on
3.  Xenotransplantation                     :  Uses animal organs for transplantation
4.  Tissue Engineering                      :  Creates artificial tissues and organs
5.  Gene silencing                         :  Used in cancer treatment


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5
(d) 1, 2, and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All five pairs accurately reflect the applications of the listed medical technologies. CAR T-cell therapy is used to treat some leukemias and lymphomas. MRT aims to prevent the inheritance of mitochondrial diseases. Xenotransplantation involves transplanting animal organs into humans. Tissue engineering creates artificial tissues and organs. Gene silencing is a therapeutic strategy used in the treatment of various diseases, including cancer.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Pollutant                       Source/Association
1. Sulphur dioxide                 :   Wet scrubbers
2. Heavy metals                    :   E-waste
3. Carbon monoxide                :   Coal-fired power plants

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Wet scrubbers are a technology specifically designed to remove sulphur dioxide from industrial emissions, primarily from coal-fired power plants.  Therefore, pair 1 is correctly matched. E-waste, comprising discarded electronic devices, contains significant quantities of heavy metals like lead, mercury, and cadmium.  The improper disposal of e-waste leads to the leaching of these heavy metals into the environment, thus pair 2 is correct.  While coal-fired power plants do emit carbon monoxide, it's not their sole or primary association.  Other sources, such as vehicle exhaust and incomplete combustion, contribute significantly to carbon monoxide pollution. Therefore, pair 3 is incorrectly matched because it presents a limited and not the most prominent source of carbon monoxide. Option (b) accurately reflects the correct pairings. Options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they either include or exclude pairings that are not entirely accurate based on the primary and most significant sources of these pollutants.  The question tests the understanding of the specific sources and mitigation techniques associated with different pollutants.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Material                         Application/Property
1. Steel slag                       :   Production of cement
2. Graphene                        :   High surface area
3. Tantalum                         :   High corrosion resistance

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Steel slag, a byproduct of steelmaking, finds application in various industries, including as a component in cement production.  Its chemical composition lends itself to this use.  Graphene, a form of carbon, is known for its exceptionally high surface area, a property that makes it useful in various applications, including energy storage and sensors. Tantalum is a metal prized for its high corrosion resistance and high melting point, making it suitable for applications in electronics and chemical processing. All three pairs accurately reflect the properties and applications of the given materials. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they omit at least one correctly matched pair, demonstrating a lack of complete understanding of the properties and uses of these materials.  This question tests the candidate's knowledge of material science and industrial applications.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Disease                            Transmission/Characteristic
1. Hepatitis B virus                  :   Similar transmission to HIV
2. Hepatitis C                        :   No vaccine available
3. HIV                                :   Treated with monoclonal antibodies

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Hepatitis B virus, like HIV, is transmitted through bodily fluids, making their transmission routes similar.  Hepatitis C, unlike Hepatitis B, currently lacks a widely available and effective vaccine.  HIV, while not curable, can be effectively managed with antiretroviral therapy, including treatments that utilize monoclonal antibodies.  Therefore, all three pairs are correctly matched. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect as they fail to identify the accurate matching of all three pairs, indicating an incomplete understanding of the diseases and their characteristics. The question assesses the candidate's understanding of infectious diseases, their transmission, and treatment modalities.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Technology/Process                  Application/Outcome
1. AMRIT technology                   :   Arsenic removal from water
2. Algae Assisted Fuel Cells (AFC)  :   Carbon dioxide capture
3.  Hyperloop                         :   Ultra-high-speed transportation

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

AMRIT (Arsenic Mitigation through Remediation of Impacted Trenches) technology, developed by IIT Madras, is specifically designed for removing arsenic and other metal ions from contaminated water sources.  Algae Assisted Fuel Cells (AFC) leverage algae's ability to absorb carbon dioxide, offering a sustainable approach to carbon capture and wastewater treatment while simultaneously generating power.  Hyperloop technology aims to create an ultra-high-speed ground transportation system, significantly faster than conventional rail or air travel. All three pairs accurately reflect the application and outcome of the technologies mentioned. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they fail to recognize the accurate pairing of all three technologies with their respective applications and outcomes. This question tests the candidate's knowledge of emerging technologies and their applications in addressing environmental and infrastructural challenges.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Pollutant/Substance                Environmental Impact/Effect
1. White phosphorus                  :   Severe burns
2. Supercritical carbon dioxide     :   Enhanced oil recovery
3. Mercury                           :   Neurological damage

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

White phosphorus, when ignited, causes severe burns due to its incendiary properties.  Supercritical carbon dioxide is used in enhanced oil recovery techniques to extract more oil from depleted reservoirs. Mercury is a neurotoxin, causing significant neurological damage through its impact on the nervous system.  Therefore, all three pairs accurately link the substance/pollutant to its environmental impact or effect. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they incorrectly exclude at least one correctly matched pair.  This question assesses the candidate's knowledge of hazardous substances and their environmental and health consequences.  It tests factual recall and the ability to link cause and effect.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

Disease                     Transmission Method
1. Hepatitis B                : Blood transfusion
2. HIV                         : Sexual contact
3. Hepatitis C                : Sharing needles
4.  Influenza A (H1N1)       : Airborne droplets


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Hepatitis B can be transmitted through various routes, including blood transfusions, sexual contact, and sharing needles. HIV is primarily transmitted through sexual contact, blood transfusions, and sharing needles. Hepatitis C is most commonly transmitted through sharing needles contaminated with infected blood. Influenza A (H1N1), commonly known as swine flu, is spread through airborne droplets produced when an infected person coughs or sneezes. Therefore, all pairs (1, 2, and 3) are correctly matched.  Option (a) is incorrect as it only includes Hepatitis B, neglecting the accurate transmission routes of HIV and Hepatitis C. Option (b) is partially correct in mentioning Hepatitis B and HIV but omits Hepatitis C. Option (c) is also partially correct in that it correctly matches HIV and Hepatitis C, but it fails to account for Hepatitis B transmission.  The question tests factual recall of disease transmission methods, requiring the candidate to possess detailed knowledge of the various routes of infection for different viral diseases.


**2. With reference to viral infections, consider the following pairs:**

Virus                       Associated Disease
1.  Human Immunodeficiency Virus (HIV) :  Cirrhosis
2.  Hepatitis B Virus (HBV)             :  Liver cancer
3.  Hepatitis C Virus (HCV)             : AIDS


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Human Immunodeficiency Virus (HIV) causes Acquired Immunodeficiency Syndrome (AIDS), not cirrhosis.  Cirrhosis is a late-stage liver disease most commonly caused by chronic alcohol abuse, Hepatitis B and Hepatitis C. Hepatitis B Virus (HBV) can lead to liver cancer as a long-term complication. Hepatitis C Virus (HCV) primarily causes liver damage and cirrhosis, eventually leading to liver cancer; it does not cause AIDS.  Therefore, only pair 2 is correctly matched. Option (a) is incorrect because it incorrectly links HIV to cirrhosis. Option (b) is incorrect because it incorrectly pairs HIV with cirrhosis and omits the correct link between Hepatitis C and liver cancer. Option (d) is incorrect because it includes the incorrect pairings of 1 and 3. The question assesses factual recall and the ability to distinguish between closely related diseases and their causative agents, demanding precise knowledge of viral infections and their associated complications.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

Viral Disease          Vaccine Availability
1. Hepatitis A             : Available
2. Hepatitis B             : Not Available
3. Hepatitis C             : Available
4. HIV                     : Available


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Vaccines are available for Hepatitis A and Hepatitis B.  There is currently no vaccine for Hepatitis C or HIV.  Therefore, only pairs 1 and 3 are correctly matched. Option (a) is incorrect as it only includes Hepatitis A. Option (c) is incorrect because it incorrectly states that there are no vaccines for Hepatitis B and HIV.  Option (d) is incorrect as it incorrectly includes all the pairs. This question tests factual knowledge about vaccine availability for specific viral diseases. The inclusion of plausible distractors (incorrect vaccine availability status) makes the question challenging and assesses the candidate's ability to differentiate between accurate and inaccurate information concerning public health measures.


**4. With reference to the prevalence of viral infections, consider the following pairs:**

Viral Infection      Global Infection Numbers (Relative to HIV)
1. Hepatitis B          : Significantly Higher
2. Hepatitis C          : Significantly Lower
3.  Influenza A (H1N1) : Comparable


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Globally, the number of people infected with Hepatitis B and C viruses are significantly higher than those infected with HIV. Influenza A(H1N1) has a global prevalence that varies year to year, but it is generally considered to infect a larger number of people than HIV.   Therefore, only pair 1 is correctly matched. Option (b) is incorrect as it incorrectly includes Influenza A (H1N1). Option (c) is incorrect as it incorrectly states that Hepatitis C infections are significantly lower than HIV. Option (d) is incorrect as it includes all three incorrect pairings.  This question tests the candidate's understanding of the relative global prevalence of different viral infections compared to HIV, demanding a grasp of epidemiological data.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

Disease                     Treatment Modality
1. Hepatitis B                : Antiviral medications
2. HIV                         : Antiretroviral therapy
3. Hepatitis C                :  Antiviral medications
4. Influenza A (H1N1)       : Antiviral medications (in severe cases)


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Hepatitis B is treated with antiviral medications to suppress viral replication and prevent liver damage. HIV is managed with antiretroviral therapy (ART), a combination of drugs that target different stages of the viral life cycle.  Hepatitis C is also treated with antiviral medications, targeting specific viral proteins. Influenza A (H1N1) is typically treated with rest and supportive care, but antiviral medications might be prescribed in severe cases to reduce the duration and severity of illness.  Therefore, all four pairs are correctly matched. Options (a), (b), and (c) are all partially correct, but they exclude at least one correctly matched pair.  This question assesses factual recall of treatment modalities for various viral infections, demanding knowledge of specific medical interventions.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Organism                     Habitat
1. Algae                         Tundra
2. Fungi                         Coral Reefs
3. Phytoplankton                Estuaries
4. Lichens                       Bare Rock

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 2 and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Algae are found in a wide variety of habitats, including aquatic environments like estuaries and even some terrestrial environments, but the tundra is not a primary habitat for algae.  Fungi are found in diverse locations, including coral reefs, but their presence is not exclusive to this environment.  Phytoplankton, which are microscopic algae, are indeed a major component of estuarine ecosystems. Lichens, a symbiotic association of algae and fungi, are highly adaptable and are known for their ability to colonize inhospitable environments like bare rocks, initiating ecological succession. Therefore, only pairs 3 and 4 are correctly matched.  Option (a) is incorrect as algae are not primarily associated with tundra environments. Option (b) is partially correct but incomplete. Option (d) is incorrect because while fungi are found in diverse locations (including within lichens that thrive on bare rock), they are not exclusively found in coral reefs.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Biological Process            Organism/Entity
1. Photosynthesis               Fungi
2. Respiration                  Algae
3. Ecological Succession        Lichens
4. Mineral Enrichment           Algae

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 and 4 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Photosynthesis, the process of converting light energy into chemical energy, is primarily carried out by plants and certain other organisms like algae, not fungi. Fungi are heterotrophic organisms, obtaining energy by breaking down organic matter. Respiration, the process of releasing energy from organic molecules, occurs in all living organisms, including algae.  Ecological succession, the gradual process of community change, is often initiated by pioneer species like lichens, which can colonize bare rock. Algae contribute significantly to mineral enrichment in aquatic ecosystems through their life cycles and decomposition. Therefore, options 3 and 4 are correctly matched. Option (a) is incorrect because fungi do not perform photosynthesis. Option (c) is partially correct but incomplete. Option (d) is incorrect because fungi do not perform photosynthesis.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Biological Entity          Role/Characteristic
1. Algae                       Provides shelter to fungi
2. Fungi                       Provides food to algae
3. Lichen                       Symbiotic association with bacteria


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) None of the above

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

In a lichen, the fungal partner (mycobiont) provides structural support and protection from harsh environmental conditions to the algal partner (phycobiont).  The algal partner, through photosynthesis, produces food (carbohydrates) which is then utilized by the fungus.  Lichens are a symbiotic association of algae and fungi, not bacteria. Therefore, options 1 and 2 are correctly matched. Option (a) and (b) are partially correct, but incomplete. Option (d) is incorrect because two of the pairs are correctly matched.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

    Biofuel Source             Biofuel Type
1. Algae                       First Generation Biofuel
2. Algae                       Third Generation Biofuel
3. Plants                      Second Generation Biofuel


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

First-generation biofuels are derived from traditional food crops like corn and sugarcane. Second-generation biofuels are produced from non-food biomass sources like agricultural residues and wood.  Third-generation biofuels utilize algae as a feedstock, which offers advantages in terms of high lipid content and rapid growth rates. Therefore, only pairs 2 and 3 are correctly matched. Option (a) is incorrect because algae are not a primary source for first-generation biofuels. Option (b) is partially correct but incomplete. Option (d) is incorrect because algae are not a primary source for first-generation biofuels.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Biological Group           Higher Classification
1. Fungi                       Bacteria
2. Phytoplankton             Algae
3. Microbiome                 Fungi


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Fungi are a distinct kingdom of organisms, separate from bacteria.  Phytoplankton are a type of algae, specifically the microscopic algae that live in aquatic environments.  A microbiome is a complex community of microorganisms, which includes various types of organisms such as bacteria, fungi, and others. Therefore, only pairs 2 and 3 are correctly matched. Option (a) is incorrect because fungi are not a type of bacteria. Option (b) is partially correct but incomplete. Option (d) is incorrect because fungi are not a type of bacteria.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Force/Process                                   Related Entity
1. Gravity                                          :   Continental Drift
2. Refraction                                       :   Atmosphere
3. Radioactivity                                    :   Potassium
4. Nuclear Fission                               :    Earth's Mantle
5.  Oxidation                                      :    Iron


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Gravity is a contributing force to continental drift, a geological process involving the movement of tectonic plates.  Refraction, the bending of light, is significantly influenced by the Earth's atmosphere.  Radioactivity, the spontaneous emission of radiation, involves the decay of radioactive isotopes, including potassium.  Nuclear fission, the splitting of atomic nuclei, occurs naturally in the Earth's mantle, although at a much lower rate than in nuclear reactors. Oxidation is a chemical reaction involving the loss of electrons, and Iron readily undergoes oxidation. Therefore, pairs 1, 2, and 3 are correctly matched. Pair 4 is partially correct, as nuclear fission does occur in the Earth's mantle, but the question seeks a direct and primary relationship; the primary association of nuclear fission is with technology and not with a natural geological process. Pair 5 is correctly matched.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Element/Mineral                                 Associated Feature
1. Calcium                                        :   Desert Soils
2. Iron                                           :   Magnetite
3. Sodium                                         :    Earth's Crust
4. Boron (B)                                      :   Calcium Uptake
5. Sulphur                                        :   Reacts with Iron


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Calcium is a major component of many desert soils.  Iron is a key constituent of Magnetite, a common iron ore.  Sodium is one of the most abundant elements in the Earth's crust. Boron affects the uptake of Calcium in plants. Sulphur reacts with iron to form iron sulfide, a brittle compound. All the given pairs are correctly matched.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Process/Phenomenon                         Associated Description
1. Refraction                                   :   Daylight Extension
2. Gravity                                      :   Black Holes
3.  Nuclear Fission                            :   Small Modular Reactors (SMRs)
4.  Radioactivity                               :   Uranium
5.  Ocean Currents                             :   Gravity


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Atmospheric refraction extends daylight by bending sunlight, making the sun appear above the horizon even after it has technically set. Black holes are characterized by their immense gravitational pull. Small Modular Reactors (SMRs) utilize nuclear fission for power generation. Radioactivity involves the decay of unstable isotopes like uranium. Ocean currents are initiated and influenced by gravity.  Therefore, all the pairs are correctly matched.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Material/Substance                           Characteristic/Property
1. Iron                                          :   Good Conductor
2. Zinc                                          :   Protects Iron from Corrosion
3.  Vanadium                                     :   Vanadium Flow Batteries
4.  Lab-grown Diamonds                         :  High-Pressure, High-Temperature (HPHT) synthesis
5.  Methanol                                    :   Direct Methanol Fuel Cells (DMFCs)


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Iron is a good conductor of electricity and heat. Zinc is used as a protective coating for iron to prevent corrosion (galvanization). Vanadium is a key component in vanadium flow batteries, a type of energy storage technology. Lab-grown diamonds are often synthesized using High-Pressure, High-Temperature (HPHT) methods. Methanol is the fuel used in Direct Methanol Fuel Cells (DMFCs).  All of the pairs are correctly matched.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Technology/Process                            Application/Use
1.  Genome Editing                               :   Low-pungent Mustard
2.  Tissue Culture                              :   Propagation of Rare Trees
3.  GPS Spoofing                                 :   Disrupting Navigation Systems
4.  White Rabbit Technology                     :   High-precision Synchronization
5.  Satellite Communication Technology (SCT)   :   Direct Satellite Calls



Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4 and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)


**Explanation:**

Genome editing techniques have been used to create low-pungent mustard varieties. Tissue culture is a common method for propagating plants, including rare and endangered tree species. GPS spoofing involves transmitting false GPS signals to disrupt navigation systems. White Rabbit technology is used in applications requiring high-precision synchronization, such as particle accelerators. Satellite communication technology enables direct satellite calls, eliminating the need for terrestrial infrastructure in certain cases.  Therefore, all five pairs are correctly matched.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Nuclear Technology                Associated Feature
1. Pressurized Heavy Water Reactor (PHWR) : Uses enriched uranium as fuel
2. Fast Breeder Reactor (FBR)          :  Employs liquid sodium as coolant
3. Small Modular Reactor (SMR)        : Primarily utilizes thorium as fuel

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only the second pair is correctly matched. Fast Breeder Reactors (FBRs) indeed utilize liquid sodium as a coolant, offering advantages in heat transfer efficiency.  PHWRs, on the other hand, use natural or slightly enriched uranium, not highly enriched uranium.  The use of enriched uranium is more common in other reactor types like Light Water Reactors (LWRs).  Finally, while SMRs are a developing technology with potential for various fuel types, they are not *primarily* reliant on thorium.  Thorium-based reactors represent a separate and distinct advanced reactor technology, often categorized as "Generation IV" reactors. The use of thorium is being explored in various reactor designs, but SMRs are not exclusively or primarily designed around thorium fuel.  Therefore, only the statement about the FBR's coolant is accurate.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Nuclear Fuel                     Characteristic
1. Uranium                           :  Abundant in India's monazite sands
2. Thorium                           :   Directly sustains a nuclear chain reaction
3. Plutonium-239                    :  Produced in Fast Breeder Reactors

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Only the third pair is correctly matched. Plutonium-239 is a fissile material produced as a byproduct in Fast Breeder Reactors (FBRs) through the breeding process.  The first pair is incorrect because while uranium is found in India, it's primarily found in different geological formations, not specifically and abundantly in monazite sands. Monazite is a significant source of thorium.  The second pair is incorrect because thorium itself is not a fissile material; it's a fertile material that needs to be converted into a fissile isotope (like Uranium-233) before it can sustain a chain reaction. Thus, only the statement regarding Plutonium-239's production in FBRs is factually accurate.



**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Nuclear Reactor Type             Key Feature
1.  Pressurized Water Reactor (PWR) : Uses heavy water as a moderator
2.  Boiling Water Reactor (BWR)    :  Water acts as both coolant and moderator
3.  Small Modular Reactor (SMR)    :  Designed for on-site construction only


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only the second pair is correct. Boiling Water Reactors (BWRs) utilize water as both the coolant (to remove heat) and the moderator (to slow down neutrons for efficient fission).  The first pair is incorrect because PWRs use ordinary (light) water as a coolant and may use light water or heavy water as a moderator depending on design.  The third pair is incorrect because a key advantage of SMRs is their factory-fabricated modular design, allowing for off-site construction and easier transportation to various locations. Therefore, only the statement describing the BWR's dual role of water as coolant and moderator is accurate.


**4. With reference to nuclear energy, consider the following pairs:**

   Concept                                 Description
1.  Nuclear Fission                          :  The fusion of atomic nuclei
2.  Nuclear Fusion                           : The splitting of atomic nuclei
3.  Critical Mass                             : The minimum amount of fissile material needed for a sustained chain reaction

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Only the third pair is correctly matched. A critical mass is indeed the minimum amount of fissile material (like uranium-235 or plutonium-239) required to initiate and sustain a self-propagating chain reaction of nuclear fission.  The first two pairs are reversed. Nuclear fission is the splitting of an atomic nucleus, while nuclear fusion is the combining of atomic nuclei. Therefore, only the definition of critical mass is accurate.

(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Explanation:**

All three pairs are correctly matched. The stratosphere contains the ozone layer, which absorbs harmful ultraviolet radiation from the sun. The troposphere, being the lowest layer, contains the highest concentration of greenhouse gases, which contribute to the Earth's climate. **6. Consider the following pairs:**

   Material                                  Property

2.  Graphite                               : Acts as a moderator in some reactors
3.  Liquid Sodium                           : Used as a coolant in some reactors


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Pairs 2 and 3 are correctly matched. Graphite is used as a neutron moderator in some nuclear reactors to slow down neutrons for improved fission efficiency. Liquid sodium is used as a coolant in certain reactor designs, particularly Fast Breeder Reactors (FBRs), due to its excellent heat transfer properties.  However, the first pair is incorrect: heavy water (deuterium oxide) acts as a *moderator*, slowing down neutrons, not increasing their speed.  Therefore, only the statements about graphite and liquid sodium are accurate.

**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Atmospheric Layer                   Characteristic Feature

(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3 and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Ionosphere's ability to reflect radio waves is due to the ionization of its gases by solar radiation, not primarily ozone concentration.  Ozone is a significant component of the stratosphere. The Thermosphere does indeed contain the Ionosphere as a layer within it.  The Exosphere is located above the Ionosphere, not below. Earthquakes can indirectly affect the Magnetosphere by causing disturbances in the Earth's magnetic field, however this is not a direct or primary characteristic of the magnetosphere. **3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Organization                          Action related to Aspartame
1. FSSAI                               :   Classified Aspartame as possibly carcinogenic
2. IARC                                :   Approved Aspartame for use in food products
3. WHO                                 :   Set daily intake limits for Aspartame

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Food Safety and Standards Authority of India (FSSAI) approves the use of Aspartame within certain limits, not classifies it as possibly carcinogenic. That classification falls under the International Agency for Research on Cancer (IARC). The IARC classifies Aspartame as "possibly carcinogenic to humans," meaning there is limited evidence of carcinogenicity in humans but sufficient evidence in animals to suggest a possible risk.  The World Health Organization (WHO) sets acceptable daily intakes (ADIs) for various substances, including Aspartame, based on scientific evaluations of safety data. Therefore, only pair 3 accurately describes a WHO action concerning Aspartame. The question tests the candidate's understanding of the roles of different international organizations in regulating food additives and their specific actions regarding Aspartame. The distractors are designed to test the candidate's knowledge of the different mandates of these organizations.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Chemical Species                     Effect on Ozone
1. Free Radicals                        :   Depletes ozone
2. Chlorofluorocarbons (CFCs)         :   Enhances ozone
3. Nitrogen Oxides (NOx)              :   Depletes ozone
4. Methane                              :   Enhances ozone

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 and 4 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Free radicals, particularly those containing chlorine and bromine atoms, catalytically destroy ozone molecules in the stratosphere. Nitrogen oxides (NOx) also contribute to ozone depletion, particularly in the troposphere, though their impact is more complex than that of CFCs.  CFCs and methane are potent greenhouse gases but are not directly linked to enhancing ozone. In fact, methane contributes to tropospheric ozone formation, which is a pollutant, not a protective ozone layer.  Therefore, only pairs 1 and 3 are correctly matched. The question assesses the candidate's understanding of the chemical processes involved in ozone depletion and the role of various chemical species in this process, requiring a deep understanding of atmospheric chemistry.  The distractors are designed to test the candidate's ability to distinguish between different types of atmospheric pollutants and their effects.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

Atmospheric Layer             Associated Phenomenon
1. Ionosphere                     :  Reflection of radio waves
2. Stratosphere                   :  Absorption of UV radiation
3. Thermosphere                   :  Presence of charged particles
4. Exosphere                      :  Gradual transition to outer space
5. Mesosphere                    :  Meteor burning


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 2, and 3 only

**Explanation:**

The Ionosphere contains charged particles that reflect radio waves back to Earth, facilitating long-distance radio communication. This is a well-established fact in atmospheric science.  The Stratosphere contains a high concentration of ozone, which absorbs a significant portion of the sun's harmful ultraviolet (UV) radiation, protecting life on Earth. The Thermosphere is characterized by extremely high temperatures due to the absorption of high-energy solar radiation, leading to ionization of atmospheric gases.  The Exosphere is the outermost layer, where the atmosphere gradually fades into outer space; there isn't a single defining phenomenon.  The Mesosphere is characterized by the burning up of meteors due to friction with atmospheric gases. Therefore, options 1, 2, and 3 are correctly matched. Option 4 is partially correct in that the Exosphere marks a transition to space but is not a uniquely defining feature. Option 5 is correctly matched.

(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 4 and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (c) 2 and 4 only

The stratosphere's altitude range is approximately 10-50 km, and the thermosphere extends from roughly 80-600 km.  The troposphere extends from the surface to about 10-12 km, depending on latitude and season. The mesosphere's altitude is typically 50-85 km. The exosphere begins above the thermosphere, generally considered to start above 600 km.  Therefore, only pairs 2 and 4 are correctly matched.  The other pairs present incorrect altitude ranges.

Ozone Layer Characteristic       Description

(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5

Ozone depletion leads to increased UV radiation reaching the Earth's surface, causing various harmful effects.
