**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Material                     Location of Significant Reserves
1. Thorium                      Australia
2. Uranium                      Rajasthan, India
3. Thorium                      Kerala Coast, India
4. Uranium                      Katanga Plateau

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2, 3 and 4

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

India possesses significant thorium reserves, notably along the Kerala coast.  Australia also has substantial thorium deposits. Rajasthan is a known region in India for uranium mining. The Katanga Plateau in the Democratic Republic of Congo is historically significant for its substantial uranium reserves. Therefore, pairs 2 and 3 are correctly matched. Pair 1 is correct as Australia holds significant Thorium reserves. However, pair 4 is a distractor because while uranium is found globally, the Katanga Plateau is known for its copper reserves as well as significant uranium deposits.  The question tests the candidate's knowledge of the geographical distribution of these crucial atomic minerals, highlighting the strategic importance of these resources for various nations.  The inclusion of plausible yet incorrect options (like focusing on a specific region for uranium, when it's found globally) adds to the question's difficulty and assesses the candidate's ability to differentiate between accurate and partially correct information.

**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Material                    Use in Technology
1. Thorium                     Fast Breeder Reactors
2. Uranium                     Thorium reactors
3. Uranium                     Nuclear Power Plants in India
4. Thorium                     Molten Salt Reactors (MSRs)

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3 and 4

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Uranium is currently the primary fuel used in India's nuclear power plants.  Thorium reactors, while being developed, utilize thorium as their fuel. Fast breeder reactors primarily use uranium or plutonium. Molten salt reactors (MSRs) are a type of reactor design that is being explored for its potential to utilize thorium as fuel. Thus, pairs 3 and 4 are correctly matched.  Pairs 1 and 2 are incorrect because they misrepresent the primary fuel source for each reactor type. This question tests knowledge of different reactor types and their fuel sources, highlighting the ongoing research and development in nuclear technology, specifically concerning thorium's potential role.  The distractors are designed to test if a candidate can accurately distinguish between the current prevalent technology and the future potential application of thorium.

**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Material                  Source Mineral
1. Thorium                   Pitchblende
2. Thorium                   Monazite
3. Uranium                   Monazite
4. Uranium                   Thorianite

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3 and 4

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Thorium is primarily extracted from monazite sands.  Uranium is found in various minerals, including thorianite. Pitchblende is primarily a source of uranium, not thorium.  Monazite contains thorium but also other elements like uranium. Therefore, only pairs 2 and 4 are correctly matched. This question tests the candidates knowledge of the sources of thorium and uranium, requiring an understanding of mineralogy and the extraction process of these radioactive elements.  The incorrect pairs are carefully chosen to include minerals associated with either thorium or uranium, creating plausible yet incorrect matches to assess the candidates ability to recall specific mineral-element pairings.


**4. With reference to Thorium and Uranium, consider the following pairs:**

   Property                     Thorium                                  Uranium
1. Abundance                   More abundant than uranium                 Less abundant than thorium
2. Radioactivity               Contributes to natural terrestrial radioactivity  Contributes to natural terrestrial radioactivity
3. Waste Production           Produces less harmful waste                 Produces more harmful waste

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Thorium is significantly more abundant in the Earth's crust than uranium. Both thorium and uranium are radioactive elements that contribute to natural terrestrial radioactivity.  Thorium-based reactors generally produce less long-lived and harmful radioactive waste compared to uranium-based reactors. All three pairs accurately reflect the properties and characteristics of thorium and uranium, demonstrating a comprehensive understanding of the differences and similarities between these two elements.  The correct answer is (d) because all three statements present a factually accurate comparison between thorium and uranium.  The question assesses the candidates knowledge of the relative abundance, radioactivity, and waste production characteristics of these key nuclear materials.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   State                      Known for Thorium Production
1. Rajasthan                  Significant Thorium Reserves
2. Kerala                      Significant Thorium Reserves
3. Tamil Nadu                 Significant Thorium Reserves
4. Jharkhand                  Significant Uranium Reserves

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 4 only
(d) 2, 3 and 4


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Kerala and Tamil Nadu are known for their significant monazite sand deposits, which are a major source of thorium. While Rajasthan has uranium deposits, it is not primarily known for thorium production. Jharkhand is known for its uranium deposits.  Therefore, only pairs 2 and 3 are correctly matched.  The question tests the candidate's knowledge of the geographical distribution of thorium resources within India, specifically focusing on states known for their thorium production.  The distractors include states known for other mineral resources, testing the candidates ability to accurately associate specific states with their primary mineral production.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  The questions are designed to be challenging and test various cognitive skills, particularly factual recall and analytical ability.  Note that the difficulty level is subjective and might vary based on the examinee's background.


**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Atmospheric Layer           Characteristic Feature
1. Stratosphere                 :   Presence of Polar Stratospheric Clouds
2. Ozone Layer                  :   Located in the troposphere
3. Lower Stratosphere           :   Characterized by a positive lapse rate
4. Stratosphere                 :   Location of the SOFIA project operations


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 4 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The correct answer is (b) because Polar Stratospheric Clouds (PSCs) are indeed a characteristic feature of the stratosphere, and the Stratospheric Observatory for Infrared Astronomy (SOFIA) operated within the stratosphere. Option 1 is correct. Option 4 is also correct.

Option 2 is incorrect: The ozone layer is primarily located in the stratosphere, not the troposphere.  The troposphere is the lowest layer of the atmosphere.

Option 3 is incorrect: The lower stratosphere is characterized by a negative lapse rate, meaning temperature increases with altitude, unlike the troposphere where temperature decreases with altitude.  This temperature inversion is crucial for the stability of the stratosphere and the concentration of ozone.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Country                      Specific Action Regarding India
1. USA                           :   Opposed India's membership in the Australia Group
2. USA                           :   Supported India's NSG membership bid
3. India                          :   Sought assistance from the USA for specific technologies.


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Only pair 3 is correctly matched. India has repeatedly sought technological assistance from the USA in various sectors, including defense and space.

Pair 1 is incorrect.  The USA has, in recent years, supported India's membership in various export control regimes, including the Australia Group.

Pair 2 is factually complex and requires nuance. While the US has generally supported India's aspirations for greater participation in nuclear export control groups, the NSG membership bid has a long and complex history with varying levels of support from different US administrations and at different times.  Therefore, a simple "supported" is an oversimplification and inaccurate for a definitive matching.


**3. Consider the following statements:**

  Statement related to the Stratosphere
1. The stratosphere contains the ozone layer, which absorbs harmful ultraviolet radiation.
2. Jet aircraft fly smoothly in the lower stratosphere due to the absence of significant vertical winds.
3. The stratosphere is characterized by a temperature inversion, where temperature increases with altitude.
4. Polar stratospheric clouds are a phenomenon exclusive to the troposphere.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1, 2, and 3 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statements 1, 2, and 3 are all correct descriptions of aspects of the stratosphere. The ozone layer's presence and its UV absorption are well-established. The smooth flight of jet aircraft in the lower stratosphere is attributed to the stable atmospheric conditions, including the lack of significant vertical winds. The temperature inversion is a defining characteristic of the stratosphere.

Statement 4 is incorrect. Polar stratospheric clouds (PSCs) are indeed found in the stratosphere, a crucial aspect of ozone depletion processes in polar regions.  They are not found in the troposphere.


**4.  With reference to the impact of the USA on India, consider the following pairs:**

   Area of Impact                     Specific Example
1.  Technology Transfer               :   Provision of  F-16 fighter jets to India
2.  Economic Relations                :   Imposition of sanctions under CAATSA
3.  Strategic Partnerships            :   Joint military exercises like Malabar


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)


**Explanation:**

Pairs 2 and 3 are correctly matched.  The US has imposed sanctions on countries under the Countering America's Adversaries Through Sanctions Act (CAATSA), and this has impacted India's relations with the US. The Malabar exercises are a key example of the growing strategic partnership between India and the USA.

Pair 1 is incorrect: The USA has not supplied F-16 fighter jets to India.  India's fighter jet acquisitions have primarily involved other countries.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

    Atmospheric Phenomenon        Location
1. Polar Cyclones                 : Extend to the troposphere only
2. Polar Stratospheric Clouds     :  Stratosphere
3. Negative Lapse Rate            :  Troposphere


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)


**Explanation:**

Only pair 2 is correctly matched. Polar stratospheric clouds are a phenomenon that occurs in the stratosphere.

Pair 1 is incorrect: Polar cyclones extend into the stratosphere, influencing stratospheric dynamics and ozone chemistry.

Pair 3 is incorrect: A negative lapse rate, where temperature increases with altitude, is characteristic of the stratosphere, not the troposphere. The troposphere experiences a positive lapse rate (temperature decreases with altitude).

Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided target content, focusing on the European Union.  Each question adheres to the specified format and includes a detailed explanation.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Organization/Initiative            Relationship with the European Union
1.  Global Methane Pledge (GMP)       :   Major implementing partner
2.  International Methane Emissions Observatory (IMEO) :  Primary funder
3.  India-Middle East-Europe Economic Corridor (IMEC) :  Active participant

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

The European Union is a key player in global climate action and has taken a leading role in initiatives targeting methane emissions.  The Global Methane Pledge (GMP), a commitment by countries to reduce methane emissions, counts the EU as a significant implementing partner, actively working towards its goals.  Similarly, the EU is a major supporter of the International Methane Emissions Observatory (IMEO), providing substantial funding for its operations and data analysis. The IMEO's aim to track and verify methane emissions aligns directly with the EU's climate ambitions.  Finally, the European Union is an active participant in the India-Middle East-Europe Economic Corridor (IMEC), an initiative aimed at boosting trade and connectivity across the three regions.  Therefore, all three pairs are correctly matched. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they exclude at least one correctly matched pair.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Country/Organization               Relationship with the European Union
1.  Russia                           :   Member of the EU Trade and Technology Council (TTC)
2.  India                            :   Negotiating a Free Trade Agreement (FTA)
3.  FAO                              :   Formal observer status within the EU

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The relationship between the European Union and various entities requires careful consideration.  Russia shares a border with the EU but is not a member of any EU bodies. The EU Trade and Technology Council (TTC) is a body formed to address technological and trade issues, and Russia is not a member. Therefore, pair 1 is incorrect. India and the EU are actively engaged in negotiations for a comprehensive Free Trade Agreement (FTA). This is a significant bilateral undertaking, making pair 2 correct. The Food and Agriculture Organization (FAO) is a separate international organization and does not hold formal observer status within the European Union's internal structures; hence pair 3 is incorrect.  Therefore, only pair 2 is correctly matched, making (c) the correct answer. Options (a), (b), and (d) incorrectly include pairs that are mismatched.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

    Law/Policy                          Implementation Body
1.  Artificial Intelligence Act         :   European Commission
2.  Green Deal Industrial Plan         :   Member States of the EU
3.  CBAM (Carbon Border Adjustment Mechanism) :   European Parliament

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The implementation of EU laws and policies involves various actors. The Artificial Intelligence Act, a landmark piece of legislation regulating AI systems, is primarily implemented by the European Commission, the EU's executive branch, responsible for proposing and enforcing legislation.  The Green Deal Industrial Plan, a comprehensive strategy for sustainable industrial growth, is implemented through collaborative efforts involving the Member States of the EU, each responsible for its national implementation strategies.  The CBAM (Carbon Border Adjustment Mechanism), a policy to level the playing field for carbon emissions, is not primarily implemented by the European Parliament, which is the legislative branch; its implementation is primarily a Commission responsibility and involves Member States. Therefore, only pairs 1 and 2 are correctly matched. Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect as they either include the incorrectly matched pair 3 or exclude correctly matched pairs 1 and 2.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Geographic Entity                 Relationship with the European Union
1.  Ukraine                          :   EU member state
2.  Bulgaria                         :   EU member state
3.  Japan                            :   Has a free trade agreement with the EU

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Ukraine is currently an EU candidate country, actively working towards EU membership, but it is not yet a full member. Therefore, pair 1 is incorrect. Bulgaria is a full member state of the European Union. Thus, pair 2 is correct. The EU and Japan have an Economic Partnership Agreement (EPA), which essentially functions as a free trade agreement. Thus, pair 3 is correct.  Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they either include the incorrectly matched pair 1 or exclude correctly matched pairs 2 and 3.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Chemical Compound/Product          European Union Regulation
1.  Ethylene oxide                   :   Mandatory testing in agricultural imports
2.  Aspartame                         :   Banned as a food additive
3.  Biodiesel                         :   Subsidized as a renewable fuel source

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The EU has various regulations concerning chemicals and products. Ethylene oxide, a carcinogenic substance, is subject to mandatory testing in agricultural imports to the EU to ensure safety standards are met.  Therefore, pair 1 is correct. Aspartame is not banned as a food additive in the EU; it is subject to regulations on its use and labeling, but not a complete ban. Therefore, pair 2 is incorrect. Biodiesel is promoted by the EU as a renewable fuel source and often receives subsidies to encourage its use, as part of broader climate change mitigation strategies. Therefore, pair 3 is correct. Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they either exclude correctly matched pairs 1 and 3 or include the incorrectly matched pair 2.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Technology                                    Application
1.  CRISPR/Cas9 gene editing technology       :    Development of low-pungent mustard
2.  Electrolysis                               :     Production of "green" hydrogen
3.  Transesterification                         :     Conversion of vegetable oils into biodiesel
4.  Steam methane reforming                    :     Production of "grey" hydrogen


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All the pairs are correctly matched.  CRISPR/Cas9 is a gene-editing technology successfully used to create a low-pungent mustard variety by modifying glucosinolate levels. Electrolysis, the process of using electricity to split water into hydrogen and oxygen, is a key method for producing "green" hydrogen, which is considered environmentally friendly due to its reliance on renewable energy sources.  Transesterification is the chemical process used to convert vegetable oils or animal fats into biodiesel, a renewable fuel alternative to petroleum diesel. Steam methane reforming is an industrial process used to produce hydrogen from natural gas; however, this method generates significant carbon dioxide emissions, resulting in "grey" hydrogen. Therefore, option (d) encompasses all correctly matched pairs. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they exclude at least one correctly matched pair.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Satellite System                                    Characteristic
1.  Starlink                                        :    Geosynchronous orbit
2.  Tiantong-1                                      :    Enables smartphone calls without ground-based infrastructure
3.  GPS                                             :    Owned by the United States
4.  Radar-imaging satellites                       :     Observes Earth


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 2, 3, and 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Starlink satellites operate in Low Earth Orbit (LEO), not geosynchronous orbit, making pair 1 incorrect. Tiantong-1 is indeed a satellite system designed to enable direct satellite calls to smartphones without needing cellular towers, making pair 2 correct. GPS is a satellite navigation system owned and operated by the United States, making pair 3 correct. Radar-imaging satellites use radar technology to observe and map the Earth's surface, making pair 4 correct.  Therefore, only pairs 2, 3, and 4 are correctly matched. Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect because they either include the incorrectly matched pair 1 or exclude one or more of the correctly matched pairs.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Energy Source                                   Property
1.  Biodiesel                                      :   Produces significantly less particulate matter than petroleum diesel
2.  Hydrogen (produced via electrolysis)           :   Non-greenhouse gas emitter
3.  Lithium-ion batteries                           :   High energy density
4.  Sand batteries                                :   Primarily used for heating


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Biodiesel is a cleaner-burning fuel compared to petroleum diesel, producing fewer particulates, making pair 1 correct. Hydrogen produced via electrolysis, using renewable energy sources, is considered a non-greenhouse gas emitter because its combustion primarily produces water vapor, making pair 2 correct. Lithium-ion batteries are known for their high energy density, allowing them to store a significant amount of energy in a compact size, making pair 3 correct. Sand batteries leverage the thermal properties of sand to store thermal energy, primarily used for heating applications, making pair 4 correct. Therefore, all four pairs are correctly matched. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect as they exclude at least one correctly matched pair.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Material                                         Use in Technology
1.  Heavy water                                   :    Moderator in PHWRs (Pressurized Heavy Water Reactors)
2.  Liquid oxygen (LOX)                          :    Oxidizer in semi-cryogenic engines
3.  Triethylaluminum and Triethylboron           :    Start fuel ampule in SCE (Semi-Cryogenic Engine) ignition
4.  Graphite                                     :    Cathode material in lithium-ion batteries


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Heavy water is used as a neutron moderator in Pressurized Heavy Water Reactors (PHWRs), making pair 1 correct. Liquid oxygen (LOX) serves as the oxidizer in semi-cryogenic engines, a crucial component for combustion, making pair 2 correct.  Triethylaluminum and Triethylboron are used in the start fuel ampule for igniting the semi-cryogenic engine (SCE), making pair 3 correct. However, graphite is the anode material, not the cathode material, in lithium-ion batteries, making pair 4 incorrect.  Therefore, only pairs 1, 2, and 3 are correctly matched. Options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they either include the incorrectly matched pair 4 or exclude one or more of the correctly matched pairs.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Disease                                          Characteristic/Treatment
1.  Meningitis                                     :    Caused by bacteria, viruses, fungi, and parasites
2.  Avian influenza (HPAI)                        :    High mortality in infected poultry
3.  Thrombosis with Thrombocytopenia Syndrome (TTS):  Blood clots and low platelet count
4.  Type II diabetes                               :   Linked to high Glycemic Index diets


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Meningitis is an inflammation of the membranes surrounding the brain and spinal cord, caused by various pathogens including bacteria, viruses, fungi, and parasites, making pair 1 correct. Highly pathogenic avian influenza (HPAI) viruses cause severe disease and high mortality rates in infected poultry, making pair 2 correct. Thrombosis with thrombocytopenia syndrome (TTS) is characterized by the simultaneous occurrence of blood clots (thrombosis) and a low platelet count (thrombocytopenia), making pair 3 correct. Diets rich in high Glycemic Index (GI) foods are linked to an increased risk of type II diabetes due to rapid fluctuations in blood sugar levels, making pair 4 correct.  Therefore, all four pairs are correctly matched. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect as they exclude at least one correctly matched pair.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

     Rocket Engine Type             Fuel                     Oxidizer
    1. Cryogenic Engine             Liquid Hydrogen           Liquid Oxygen
    2. Semi-Cryogenic Engine       Refined Kerosene          Liquid Oxygen
    3. Solid-propellant Rocket     Ammonium Nitrate          Potassium Chlorate
    4. Liquid-propellant Rocket    Hydrazine                Nitric Acid


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Explanation:**

All four pairs represent accurate matches between rocket engine types and their respective fuels and oxidizers.  Cryogenic engines are known for their use of liquid hydrogen (fuel) and liquid oxygen (oxidizer), both requiring cryogenic storage temperatures.  Semi-cryogenic engines represent a compromise, utilizing readily storable refined kerosene as fuel while retaining liquid oxygen as the oxidizer.  Solid-propellant rockets typically employ a mixture of solid fuels and oxidizers, such as ammonium nitrate (oxidizer) and potassium chlorate (oxidizer) bound together in a solid matrix, offering immediate ignition but limited thrust control. Liquid-propellant rockets, a broader category, encompass a variety of fuel and oxidizer combinations, including hydrazine (fuel) and nitric acid (oxidizer), offering greater thrust control than solid-propellant systems but with increased complexity in storage and handling.  Therefore, all pairs are correctly matched, reflecting established principles of rocket propulsion technology.  Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they exclude one or more correctly matched pairs, failing to capture the full spectrum of accurate relationships presented.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

    Indian Space Mission          Launch Vehicle Stage      Engine Type
    1. Aryabhata                   Soviet Kosmos-3M            Solid Propellant
    2. Mission Gaganyaan           LVM3 Upper Stage           CE-20 Cryogenic
    3. PSLV POEM-2                 PSLV Fourth Stage           Solid Propellant
    4. RLV LEX                       Chinook Helicopter         None


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, and 3 only

**Explanation:**

The correct answer is (d) because pairs 1, 2, and 3 accurately reflect the information provided. Aryabhata, India's first satellite, was indeed launched using a Soviet Kosmos-3M rocket, a vehicle which utilizes solid propellant. Mission Gaganyaan, aimed at sending humans into space, will utilize the LVM3's upper stage powered by the CE-20 cryogenic engine.  The PSLV POEM-2 mission cleverly uses the spent fourth stage of the PSLV, itself a solid-propellant-based rocket, as an orbital platform.  Pair 4 is incorrect. The RLV LEX test utilized a helicopter for initial lift but the RLV itself doesn't have an engine during its autonomous landing phase.  Options (a), (b), and (c) are incomplete because they incorrectly include or exclude at least one of the correctly matched pairs. This demonstrates the importance of precise factual recall in correctly matching elements across different space mission parameters.

The Juno mission to Jupiter extensively uses gravitational assist maneuvers to adjust its trajectory and conserve fuel.  However, the provided text doesn't explicitly state that this is part of the program. The Dragonfly mission is uniquely designed as a rotorcraft, utilizing rotor technology for exploration on Titan's surface. **8. Consider the following pairs:**

    Neutrino Observatory      Location
    1. IceCube                 Antarctica
    2. Indian Neutrino          Theni, Tamil Nadu
    3. Chinas TRIDENT          South China Sea
    4. Kodaikanal Solar         Palani Hills, Tamil Nadu


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only

(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (c) 1, 3, and 4 only

**Explanation:**

IceCube is situated in Antarctica.  China's TRIDENT is being built in the South China Sea. Kodaikanal Solar Observatory is located in the Palani Hills of Tamil Nadu. The location of the Indian Neutrino Observatory is not Theni, Tamil Nadu.  Therefore, only pairs 1, 3, and 4 are correctly matched. Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect as they include the incorrectly matched pair related to the Indian Neutrino Observatory. This question assesses the applicant's knowledge of the geographical locations of various scientific observatories, emphasizing the global distribution of scientific research infrastructure and the importance of precise geographical information.

**9. Consider the following pairs:**

    Rocket Engine Type             Oxidizer                Fuel
    1. Solid-propellant Rocket     Ammonium Perchlorate     Aluminum powder
    2. Liquid-propellant Rocket    Liquid Oxygen            RP-1 kerosene
    3. Cryogenic Engine            Liquid Oxygen            Liquid Hydrogen
    4. Semi-Cryogenic Engine      Liquid Oxygen            Refined Kerosene


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Explanation:**

All four pairs correctly identify the oxidizer and fuel combinations used in different rocket engine types. Solid-propellant rockets commonly use ammonium perchlorate as an oxidizer and aluminum powder as a fuel.  Liquid-propellant rockets can utilize a variety of combinations, including liquid oxygen (oxidizer) and RP-1 kerosene (fuel). Cryogenic engines are distinguished by their use of liquid oxygen (oxidizer) and liquid hydrogen (fuel), both requiring extremely low temperatures for storage. Semi-cryogenic engines, often a compromise between cryogenic and other systems, typically employ liquid oxygen (oxidizer) and refined kerosene (fuel). The correct matching of all four pairs demonstrates a thorough understanding of rocket propulsion technologies and their fuel choices. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they exclude at least one correctly matched pair. This question tests factual knowledge of rocket propulsion technology and the chemical components involved, highlighting the importance of detailed understanding in this specialized area.

    4. UR Rao Satellite Centre         Bengaluru, Karnataka

(d) 2, 3, and 4 only

The Vikram Sarabhai Space Centre (VSSC) is located in Thiruvananthapuram (Trivandrum), Kerala. The Liquid Propulsion Systems Centre (LPSC) is situated in Bengaluru, Karnataka. This question tests the applicants knowledge of the geographical locations of key ISRO centers, showcasing understanding of the organizational structure of India's space program.  The inclusion of plausible distractors, such as listing two centers in Bengaluru, increases the difficulty level and necessitates precise factual recall.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Option (c) is correct because Hepatitis A is transmitted through the fecal-oral route, primarily via contaminated food or water, and AIDS is primarily transmitted through sexual contact, blood transfusions, and shared needles.  Option (a) is incorrect because Dengue is transmitted by Aedes mosquitoes, not Anopheles mosquitoes, which are vectors for malaria. Option (b) is partially correct as Pneumoconiosis is linked to inhaling certain dust particles, notably silica,  but the inclusion of only 2 and 3 makes it incorrect.  Option (d) is incorrect because, while it correctly identifies the transmission modes of AIDS and Hepatitis A, it wrongly associates Pneumoconiosis with a vector. **1. Consider the following pairs:**

Company                     Legal Action/Involvement
1. Monsanto                 :   Case involving the Protection of Plant Variety and Farmers Rights (PPVFR) Authority
2. Monsanto                 :   Ruled in favor of by the Supreme Court
3. Nuziveedu                 :   Involved in litigation with Monsanto
4.  Monsanto                 :   Affected by the Essential Commodities Act 1955
5.  Monsanto                 :   Case involving the Delhi High Court

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3 and 4


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Monsanto, a prominent multinational biotechnology company, has been involved in numerous legal battles and regulatory processes in India, particularly concerning its Bt cotton technology.  Option 1 is correct as Monsanto's Bt cotton technology has been a subject of contention and scrutiny by the Protection of Plant Variety and Farmers Rights (PPVFR) Authority, leading to various cases and proceedings. Option 2 is also correct; Monsanto has, in certain instances, obtained favorable rulings from the Supreme Court of India regarding its intellectual property rights and operations. Option 3 is correct because Monsanto has been involved in significant litigation with Indian companies like Nuziveedu Seeds, primarily centered on seed technology and patent disputes. Option 4 is partially correct in that Monsanto's operations in India would be indirectly impacted by the Essential Commodities Act 1955, which regulates the production, distribution, and pricing of essential commodities; however, this is a broader regulatory context and not a specific legal action. Option 5 is correct because the Delhi High Court has also been involved in cases concerning Monsanto's activities in India. Therefore, only options 1,2,3 and 5 are entirely and directly accurate.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

Product                     Company/Developer
1. Bollgard-II              :   Bayer CropScience
2. Bollgard                  :   Monsanto
3. Bt cotton seeds          :   Monsanto
4.  Bt brinjal                :   Mahyco
5.  Bt cotton                :   Syngenta

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 2, 3 and 4 only
(d) 2, 3, 4 and 5


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Monsanto was initially the primary developer and producer of Bollgard, the first commercially successful Bt cotton variety in India.  This makes options 2 and 3 correct. While Monsanto later sold its agricultural business, including the Bollgard brand, the initial development and introduction of Bt cotton seeds in India are firmly attributed to Monsanto.  Option 1 is incorrect; Bollgard-II is a later generation of Bt cotton, and while Monsanto played a role in its development, the current ownership and marketing might be different. Option 4 is incorrect as Mahyco (Maharashtra Hybrid Seeds Company) was involved in the development of Bt brinjal, though it faced significant opposition and regulatory hurdles. Option 5 is also incorrect; Syngenta is another major player in the agricultural biotechnology sector but wasn't the primary developer of Bt cotton in India.  Therefore, only options 2 and 3 are definitively correct based on the historical context of Bt cotton introduction in India.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

Court                       Monsanto-related Ruling
1. Supreme Court           :   Ruled against Monsanto on patent issues
2. Delhi High Court        :   Ruled in favor of Monsanto on certain matters
3. Delhi High Court        :   Case involving Monsanto on seed technology
4.  Supreme Court           :   Case involving Monsanto's market dominance
5.  PPVFR Authority        :   Case involving Monsanto on seed variety approval

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 3 and 5 only
(c) 2, 3 and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4 and 5


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Monsanto's involvement in Indian legal systems has been complex and multifaceted. Option 3 is correct; the Delhi High Court has handled various cases related to Monsanto's seed technology, including patent disputes and market practices.  Option 2 is correct as the Delhi High Court, in some instances, has indeed ruled in favor of Monsanto on specific legal matters. Option 5 is correct because the PPVFR Authority (Protection of Plant Variety and Farmers' Rights Authority) has been involved in cases concerning the approval and regulation of Monsanto's seed varieties, particularly Bt cotton. Option 1 is incorrect; while the Supreme Court has heard cases involving Monsanto, a blanket statement that it always ruled against them is an oversimplification. Option 4 is also incorrect as the Supreme Court's involvement wasn't solely focused on Monsanto's market dominance.  Therefore, only options 2, 3, and 5 reflect accurate and specific legal interactions between Monsanto and the Indian judicial system.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

Genetically Modified Crop        Source Bacterium/Gene
1. Bt brinjal                   :   Bacillus thuringiensis
2. Bt cotton                   :   Bacillus thuringiensis
3. Bt corn                     :   Bacillus cereus
4.  Bt papaya                   :   Bacillus thuringiensis
5.  Bt soybean                  :   Bacillus subtilis


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2 and 4 only
(c) 1, 2, 4 and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4 and 5


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The development of various Bt crops relies on the insertion of genes from *Bacillus thuringiensis* (Bt) bacteria, which produce insecticidal proteins. This makes options 1, 2, and 4 correct.  Bt brinjal, Bt cotton, and Bt papaya all utilize Bt genes for pest resistance. Option 3 is incorrect; Bt corn also uses Bt genes, but the statement incorrectly names *Bacillus cereus*.  Option 5 is incorrect; Bt soybean does not use *Bacillus subtilis*; it utilizes different genes for pest resistance. Therefore, only options 1, 2 and 4 accurately reflect the bacterial source of the insecticidal genes used in the development of these genetically modified crops.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

Law/Act                     Impact on Monsanto
1. Indian Patents Act 1970 (Section 3(j)) :   Affects Monsanto's patent rights on Bt cotton
2. Essential Commodities Act 1955           :   Directly regulates Monsanto's seed pricing
3.  Plant Variety Protection and Farmers' Rights Act, 2001:  Impacts Monsanto's seed variety registration
4.  Foreign Exchange Management Act, 1999:   Governs Monsanto's foreign investment approvals
5.  The Seeds Act, 1966                   :   Regulates labeling and quality of Monsanto's seeds.


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1, 3 and 5 only
(c) 1, 3, 4 and 5 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4 and 5


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Several Indian laws and acts have had a significant impact on Monsanto's operations in India. Option 1 is correct; Section 3(j) of the Indian Patents Act 1970, concerning inventions related to plants and animals, has been a key legal factor influencing Monsanto's patent rights on Bt cotton. Option 3 is also correct; the Plant Variety Protection and Farmers' Rights Act, 2001, directly impacts the registration and protection of seed varieties, thereby affecting Monsanto's operations. Option 5 is correct because The Seeds Act, 1966 regulates seed quality, labeling, and distribution, so it would directly impact Monsanto's seed products. Option 2 is incorrect; while the Essential Commodities Act 1955 deals with essential commodities, its impact on Monsanto's seed pricing is indirect and not a direct regulation. Option 4 is also incorrect; the Foreign Exchange Management Act, 1999, pertains to foreign exchange regulations and not specifically Monsanto's seed business. Therefore, only options 1, 3 and 5 accurately reflect the direct legal and regulatory impacts on Monsanto's activities in India.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Disease                         Inheritance Pattern/Genetic Material
1. Haemophilia                    :   Autosomal recessive inheritance
2. Diabetes                       :   Inherited via mitochondrial DNA
3. Sickle Cell Anemia             :   Sex-linked inheritance on the X chromosome


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Haemophilia is a sex-linked recessive disorder inherited via the X chromosome.  Males are more commonly affected because they only have one X chromosome.  Females can be carriers but typically do not exhibit the disease unless they inherit two affected X chromosomes. Option 1 is incorrect because it states autosomal recessive inheritance which is a different pattern of inheritance.

Diabetes is a complex condition with genetic components, but its inheritance pattern is not solely through mitochondrial DNA.  While mitochondrial dysfunction can contribute to some forms of diabetes, the majority of cases are influenced by a combination of genetic predispositions and environmental factors. It is not a simple Mendelian inheritance pattern. Option 2 is incorrect because it oversimplifies the complex genetic basis of diabetes.

Sickle cell anemia is inherited in an autosomal recessive manner, meaning an individual needs two copies of the affected gene (one from each parent) to have the disease.  The gene is located on an autosome (non-sex chromosome). Option 3 is correct as it correctly identifies the inheritance pattern of Sickle Cell Anemia.

Therefore, only pair 3 is correctly matched.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Biotechnological Process          Product
1. Hybridoma technology            :   Interferon
2. Recombinant DNA technology     :   Monoclonal Antibodies
3. Gene therapy                     :   Enzyme Replacement Therapy


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Hybridoma technology is used for the commercial production of monoclonal antibodies (mAbs), not interferon. Interferons are produced through other biotechnological methods like recombinant DNA technology. Option 1 is incorrect because it mismatches the product with the process.

Recombinant DNA technology involves the insertion of a gene into a different organism to produce a desired protein.  While it can be used for the production of many therapeutic proteins,  it's not directly related to the generation of monoclonal antibodies.  Monoclonal antibodies are produced by the hybridoma technology. Option 2 is therefore incorrect.

Enzyme replacement therapy (ERT) is a form of gene therapy that involves introducing functional enzymes into cells to compensate for deficiencies.  This is a direct application of gene therapy techniques. Option 3 is correct because it accurately reflects the application of gene therapy.

Therefore, only pair 3 is correctly matched.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Disease                     Treatment/Management Strategy
1. Diabetes                    :  National Programme for Prevention and Control of Diabetes, Cardiovascular Diseases and Stroke (NPCDCS)
2. Haemophilia                 : Oral Rehydration Therapy (ORT)
3. Rare Diseases              : Enzyme Replacement Therapy (ERT)


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The NPCDCS is a government program in India specifically designed to address diabetes, cardiovascular diseases, and stroke.  This makes pair 1 a correct match.

Oral Rehydration Therapy (ORT) is used to treat dehydration, often associated with diarrheal diseases, not haemophilia. Haemophilia is managed through various methods like factor replacement therapy, not ORT. Option 2 is incorrect.

Enzyme Replacement Therapy (ERT) is a common treatment strategy for several rare diseases where an enzyme deficiency is the underlying cause.  Many rare diseases fall under this category. Option 3 is correct.

Therefore, only pairs 1 and 3 are correctly matched.



**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Country                     Technology Procurement/Production
1. India                         :   Hybridoma technology
2. Australia                     :   Recombinant DNA technology
3. India                         :   Monoclonal antibodies


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

While India utilizes and produces monoclonal antibodies, the primary development of hybridoma technology was not solely in India.  Many countries contributed to its advancement. Option 1 is therefore an oversimplification.

Australia, like many developed nations, engages in and produces various biotechnological advancements, including recombinant DNA technology.  However,  attributing its sole production to Australia is inaccurate. Option 2 is an oversimplification.

India does procure and produce monoclonal antibodies. This is a well-established fact. Option 3 is correct.

Therefore, only pair 3 is correctly matched.  The question tests the knowledge of the specific technological development and its relationship with specific countries.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

    Food Category                  Disease Complication
1. High GI foods                  :   Haemophilia
2. High GI foods                  :   Diabetes
3. Low GI foods                   :   Diabetes


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1,2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

High Glycemic Index (GI) foods lead to rapid spikes in blood sugar levels, which can exacerbate the complications of diabetes.  This is a well-established fact in diabetes management.  Option 2 is therefore correct.

High GI foods have no direct link to haemophilia. Haemophilia is a bleeding disorder unrelated to dietary glycemic index. Option 1 is incorrect.

Low GI foods, in contrast to high GI foods, lead to slower, more gradual increases in blood sugar, which is beneficial for managing diabetes. However, the statement that low GI foods prevent diabetes is inaccurate.  Option 3 is incorrect because it implies a causal relationship that isn't entirely accurate.  While beneficial, low GI foods are part of a broader management strategy for diabetes, not a guaranteed preventative measure.

Therefore, only pair 2 is correctly matched. The question assesses the understanding of the relationship between dietary glycemic index and its impact on specific diseases.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question focuses on Malaria,  but incorporates distractors and requires factual recall and analytical skills.


**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Disease                       Causative Agent
1. Malaria                         :   Plasmodium ovale
2.  Tuberculosis                   :   Mycobacterium tuberculosis
3.  AIDS                           :   Human Immunodeficiency Virus (HIV)
4.  Malaria                         :  Plasmodium falciparum
5.  Ringworm                       :   Trichophyton rubrum

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All five pairs are correctly matched.  Plasmodium ovale and Plasmodium falciparum are both species of Plasmodium that cause malaria. Mycobacterium tuberculosis is the causative agent of tuberculosis.  HIV causes AIDS. Trichophyton rubrum is a fungus causing ringworm. The question includes distractors by mixing various infectious diseases and their causative agents, testing the candidate's ability to correctly identify the causative agents for each disease and also recall that there are multiple species of Plasmodium causing malaria.  Options (a), (b), and (c)  incorrectly exclude one or more of the correctly matched pairs.


**2. With reference to Malaria, consider the following pairs:**

   Element                       Related Aspect
1.  RTS,S/AS01 (Mosquirix)      :   Malaria Vaccine
2.  Anopheles gambiae           :   Malaria Vector
3.  Plasmodium vivax            :   Malaria Parasite
4.  National Malaria Eradication Programme :  Indian Government Initiative targeting Malaria
5.  Millennium Development Goals :  Global health initiative including Malaria


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4 and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All five pairs are correctly matched. RTS,S/AS01 (Mosquirix) is a malaria vaccine. Anopheles gambiae is a mosquito species that transmits malaria. Plasmodium vivax is one of the parasite species causing malaria. While there is a National Vector Borne Disease Control Programme (NVBDCP) in India that addresses malaria, the wording in the question is a plausible distractor as it is not precisely "National Malaria Eradication Programme". The Millennium Development Goals (MDGs) included targets for reducing malaria incidence.  The options are designed to test the candidate's knowledge of various aspects of malaria prevention and control, including vaccines, vectors, parasites, and global health initiatives. Incorrect options exclude correctly matched pairs.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Concept                         Example/Application
1.  Gene Drive Technology          :   Targeting Malaria Vectors
2.  Enzyme Replacement Therapy    :   Treating Congenital Thrombotic Thrombocytopenic Purpura
3.  Genome Sequencing             :   Mapping the Human Y Chromosome
4.  Recombinant DNA Technology    :   Creating Bt Cotton
5.  Mitochondrial Donation Therapy:   Creating a "three-parent baby"


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All five pairs represent correct applications or examples of the given concepts.  Gene drive technology aims to modify genes in organisms, often used to control populations of disease vectors like mosquitoes that transmit malaria. Enzyme replacement therapy uses engineered proteins to treat genetic diseases like cTTP. Genome sequencing helps map genomes, including the recently completed human Y chromosome. Recombinant DNA technology is used in creating genetically modified organisms (GMOs) like Bt cotton. Mitochondrial donation therapy involves using a donor's healthy mitochondria to prevent mitochondrial diseases in offspring, resulting in a "three-parent baby." The options provide distractors by including diverse biotechnology applications, testing the candidate's understanding of various techniques and their applications.  Incorrect options fail to recognize the accuracy of all the matched pairs.


**4. With reference to Malaria control initiatives, consider the following pairs:**

   Initiative                       Focus Area
1.  WHO vaccine list             :  Inclusion of Malaria Vaccines
2.  International Classification of Diseases (ICD-11) : Classification of Malaria
3.  National Vector Borne Disease Control Programme (NVBDCP) :  Malaria Prevention and Control in India

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) All three
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All three pairs are correctly matched. The WHO vaccine list includes approved malaria vaccines.  ICD-11, the international standard for disease classification, includes malaria. NVBDCP is the Indian government's program to control vector-borne diseases, including malaria.  The options test the candidate's understanding of the organizational and programmatic aspects of malaria control at international and national levels. Selecting an option other than (c) would indicate a lack of understanding of the roles of WHO, ICD, and NVBDCP in malaria control.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

    Parasite Species            Malaria Type
1. Plasmodium falciparum      :  Severe Malaria
2. Plasmodium vivax           :  Benign Tertian Malaria
3. Plasmodium malariae         :  Quartan Malaria
4. Plasmodium ovale           :  Ovale Malaria


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(a) 1,2 and 3 only
(b) 1, 2 and 4 only
(c) 1, 3 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3 and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d)

All four pairs are correctly matched.  *Plasmodium falciparum* is known to cause severe malaria, *Plasmodium vivax* causes benign tertian malaria, *Plasmodium malariae* causes quartan malaria, and *Plasmodium ovale* causes ovale malaria. This question tests the candidate's detailed knowledge of malaria parasitology. The options are designed to test the precise knowledge of the various Plasmodium species and the types of malaria they cause. Incorrect options exclude at least one correctly matched pair.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

Disease                       Treatment/Drug
1. Tuberculosis                 :   P-aminosalicylic acid
2. Leprosy                      :   Rifampicin
3. Sickle Cell Anaemia          :   Bone marrow transplant


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

P-aminosalicylic acid and Rifampicin are indeed used in the treatment of Tuberculosis and Leprosy respectively.  While P-aminosalicylic acid is an older drug used in combination therapy for tuberculosis, Rifampicin is a key component of multi-drug therapy for leprosy.  Bone marrow transplant is currently considered the only curative option for Sickle Cell Anemia, offering a potential for a complete cure by replacing the affected bone marrow with healthy cells that produce normal hemoglobin. Option (a) is incorrect because, although P-aminosalicylic acid is used in TB treatment, it's not the sole or primary treatment. Option (b) is incorrect as it only includes one correct pairing. Option (d) is incorrect because it includes the incorrect pairing of Tuberculosis and P-aminosalicylic acid as the primary treatment.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

Chemical Compound             Effect/Use
1. DDT                         :   Used as a defoliant in the Vietnam War
2. Dioxin                       :   Byproduct of plastic manufacturing
3. Isoniazid                    :   Treatment for both Tuberculosis and Leprosy


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1 and 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

DDT was infamously used as an insecticide and defoliant during the Vietnam War, leading to significant environmental and health consequences. Dioxin is a byproduct of various industrial processes, including plastic manufacturing, and is a highly toxic contaminant. Isoniazid is a primary drug used in the treatment of tuberculosis, but it is not effective against leprosy. Therefore, only the first two pairs are correctly matched. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they either include only one correct pair or incorrectly include the pairing of Isoniazid with both Tuberculosis and Leprosy treatment.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

Disease                       Mode of Transmission/Characteristic
1. Polio                        :   Faecal-oral route
2. Leprosy                      :   Droplet transmission
3. AIDS                         :   Transmitted through breast milk


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Polio is primarily transmitted through the faecal-oral route, meaning it spreads through contaminated food and water. Leprosy is spread through droplet transmission from the nose and mouth of infected individuals.  AIDS can be transmitted through various bodily fluids, including breast milk from an infected mother to her child. All three pairs accurately reflect the transmission methods or key characteristics of the diseases.  Therefore, options (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect as they exclude at least one correctly matched pair.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

Genetic Condition             Mode of Inheritance/Characteristic
1. Phenylketonuria            :   Inherited lack of an enzyme
2. Haemophilia                 :   Sex-linked inheritance
3. Sickle Cell Anaemia          :   Recessive gene expression on an autosome


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Phenylketonuria (PKU) is an inborn error of metabolism caused by the inherited lack of the enzyme phenylalanine hydroxylase. Haemophilia is a sex-linked recessive disorder, meaning the gene responsible is located on the X chromosome. Sickle cell anaemia results from the expression of a recessive gene located on an autosome, a non-sex chromosome.  All three pairs accurately describe the genetic basis of the respective conditions.  Options (a), (b), and (c) are therefore incomplete and incorrect.

Medical Text                   Disease Mentioned
1. Charakasamhita              :   Tuberculosis
2. Sushruta Samhita             :   Leprosy
3.  National Strategic Plan (NSP) & Roadmap for Leprosy (2023-27) :   Tuberculosis


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Charaka Samhita, an ancient Ayurvedic text, contains descriptions of diseases that align with the symptoms of tuberculosis.  The Sushruta Samhita, another ancient Indian medical text, includes descriptions of leprosy. The National Strategic Plan (NSP) & Roadmap for Leprosy (2023-27) is a government initiative focused on leprosy eradication, not tuberculosis.  Therefore, only pairs 1 and 2 are correctly matched. Options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they either omit correct pairings or include incorrect ones.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

Disease                     Causative Agent
1. Malaria                    :  Anopheles mosquito bite
2. Diarrhoea                  :  Arsenic contamination
3. Haemophilia                :  X chromosome abnormality


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Malaria is indeed caused by Plasmodium parasites transmitted through the bite of infected Anopheles mosquitoes.  Arsenic contamination of water sources is a well-established cause of diarrhoea.  Haemophilia is a genetic disorder linked to the X chromosome;  specifically, mutations in genes responsible for producing clotting factors VIII (Haemophilia A) or IX (Haemophilia B) located on the X chromosome lead to this condition. Therefore, all three pairs are correctly matched. Option (a), (b), and (c) are incorrect because they exclude at least one correctly matched pair.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

Disease                     Mode of Transmission/Cause
1. Botulism                  : Water-borne intoxication
2. Malaria                     : Plasmodium vivax parasite
3. Diarrhoea                  : Oral Rehydration Therapy (ORT)


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Botulism is a foodborne intoxication, not a waterborne one, caused by the neurotoxin produced by *Clostridium botulinum*.  Malaria is correctly paired with *Plasmodium vivax* as one of its causative parasites.  ORT is a treatment for diarrhoea, not its cause or mode of transmission.  Therefore, only pair 2 is correctly matched. Options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect as they include incorrectly matched pairs.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

Disease                      Treatment/Prevention

3. AIDS                         : Ionizing radiation avoidance


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

RTS,S/AS01 (Mosquirix) is a malaria vaccine, although its efficacy is limited. Fenugreek seeds have been traditionally used to help manage blood sugar levels in individuals with diabetes mellitus.  Exposure to ionizing radiation is known to increase susceptibility to various cancers and infections, including opportunistic infections common in AIDS patients. Therefore, all three pairs show a correct relationship between the disease and a measure for treatment or prevention. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incomplete and thus incorrect.

(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

Barbara McClintock's research led to the discovery of "jumping genes" (transposable elements). **1. Consider the following pairs:**

    Disease                     Transmission Route
    1. Polio                       :   Mosquito bite
    2. Hepatitis B                 :   Faecal-oral route
    3. Malaria                     :   Blood transfusion
    4. Plague                      :   Contact with infected rodents

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (d) 4 only

**Explanation:**

Polio is primarily transmitted through the faecal-oral route, not mosquito bites. Hepatitis B can be transmitted through various routes, including blood transfusion and contact with infected bodily fluids, but not primarily through the faecal-oral route. Malaria is transmitted through mosquito bites, not blood transfusions (although blood transfusions can be a route of transmission in some cases, it's not the primary vector). Plague is transmitted through contact with infected rodents or their fleas, making option 4 correct.  The question tests factual recall and the ability to differentiate between various disease transmission mechanisms.  Distractors are included to challenge the examinee's knowledge of disease vectors and routes of transmission, emphasizing the need for precise understanding and avoiding generalizations.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

    Disease                          Treatment/Vaccine
    1. Polio                           :  RTS,S/AS01 (Mosquirix)
    2. Malaria                         :  Oral polio vaccine (OPV)
    3. Hepatitis B                     :  Engerix-B

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 2 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (b) 3 only

**Explanation:**

The Oral polio vaccine (OPV) is used for Polio, not Malaria. RTS,S/AS01 (Mosquirix) and R21/Matrix-M are malaria vaccines.  Oral Rehydration Therapy (ORT) is a treatment for dehydration, often associated with diarrheal diseases, not a treatment for Tuberculosis. Engerix-B is a vaccine for Hepatitis B, making option 3 the only correctly matched pair. This question tests the candidate's knowledge of specific disease treatments and vaccines, requiring precise factual recall to differentiate between closely related medical interventions. The distractors are designed to test the candidate's understanding of the specific applications of different vaccines and therapies.

**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Atmospheric Layer                                 Characteristic
1. Ionosphere                                      :   Reflects radio waves
2. Thermosphere                                     :   Contains the Ionosphere

4. Stratosphere                                    :   Ozone layer concentration

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, 3, and 4

**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Technology/Device                              Application/Function

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 4 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 4 only

**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 only

**Explanation:**

Modems are devices that modulate and demodulate signals, enabling data transfer over telephone lines using binary signals.  A luxmeter measures light intensity, not blood pressure. **5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Disease                                         Deficiency

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Gene Editing Technique                     Associated Technology/Method
1. SDN 1                                      :   Involves alien genetic material
2. CRISPR-Cas9                               :   Site-directed nuclease (SDN)
3. Zinc Finger Nucleases (ZFNs)            :   Modification of existing genetic material
4. Transcription Activator-Like Effector Nucleases (TALENs) :  Gene silencing

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

SDN 1, and SDN 2, by definition, do *not* involve alien genetic material; therefore, pair 1 is incorrect.  CRISPR-Cas9 is a type of site-directed nuclease (SDN), making pair 2 correct.  Both ZFNs and TALENs are also types of site-directed nucleases used in gene editing, and they operate by modifying existing genetic material, making pair 3 correct.  While gene editing techniques *can* be used for gene silencing, it's not their primary or exclusive function; therefore, pair 4 is incorrect.  The correct answer is (b) because only pairs 2 and 3 accurately reflect the relationship between the gene editing technique and its associated technology or method.  Option (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they include at least one incorrectly matched pair.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Genetically Modified Crop                  Characteristic
1. Bt Cotton                                  :   Contains Cry2Ai gene for pink bollworm resistance
2. Bt Brinjal                                 :   Approved for commercial cultivation in India
3. GM Mustard (DMH-11)                     :   Derived from Bacillus thuringiensis genes
4.  Canola                                    : Contains high glucosinolates

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Bt cotton is known to contain the Cry1Ac gene, and recently research is being done on Cry2Ai to improve its resistance against pink bollworm. Hence, pair 1 is partially correct.  Bt brinjal was *not* approved for commercial cultivation in India due to concerns. Pair 2 is incorrect. GM mustard (DMH-11) contains genes from *Bacillus amyloliquefaciens*, not Bacillus thuringiensis. Pair 3 is incorrect. Canola is known for its *low* glucosinolate content, a key factor in its widespread use. Pair 4 is incorrect.  Therefore, only pair 1 has a partially correct relationship.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

    Genome Sequencing Technique             Characteristic
1. Short-read sequencing                      :   Better for assembling complex genomes like the Y chromosome
2. Long-read sequencing                       :  Fragments genome into small pieces (50-300 bases)
3. Telomere-to-Telomere (T2T) sequencing  :  Sequenced 92% of human genome in the Human Genome Project
4. Genome India Project (GIP)                : Aims to sequence 10,000 human genomes


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 4 only
(d) 2, 3, and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Short-read sequencing is better suited for applications requiring high throughput and is less effective for assembling complex, repetitive genomes.  Pair 1 is incorrect. Long-read sequencing is characterized by its ability to sequence longer DNA fragments, making it advantageous for resolving complex genomic regions. Pair 2 is incorrect. The Human Genome Project, while a landmark achievement, initially sequenced approximately 92% of the human genome. The T2T consortium completed the full 100% sequencing. Pair 3 is incorrect. The Genome India Project (GIP) indeed aims to sequence 10,000 human genomes, making pair 4 correct. Therefore, only pair 4 is correctly matched.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

    Biotechnology Application                 Description
1. Enzyme Replacement Therapy (ERT)          : Treats congenital thrombotic thrombocytopenic purpura (cTTP)
2.  Mitochondrial Donation Treatment (MDT) : Involves only two parents DNA
3. Gene Drive Technology (GDT)             : Modifies genes to alter Mendelian inheritance
4.  Recombinant DNA technology              :  Primarily used in plant breeding


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1 and 4 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

ERT, using recombinant proteins, is indeed used to treat cTTP, making pair 1 correct. MDT utilizes genetic material from three individuals (parents and a mitochondrial donor), not just two. Pair 2 is incorrect. GDT does modify genes to alter Mendelian inheritance patterns, making pair 3 correct. Recombinant DNA technology has applications beyond plant breeding, including medicine and other fields. Pair 4 is incorrect.  Therefore, only pairs 1 and 3 are correctly matched.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

    Type of RNA                                     Function
1. Messenger RNA (mRNA)                         : Carries genetic information from DNA to ribosomes for protein synthesis
2. Transfer RNA (tRNA)                           :  Involved in RNA interference (RNAi) pathway
3. Ribosomal RNA (rRNA)                          :  Forms structural and catalytic components of ribosomes
4. Small interfering RNA (siRNA)                 :   Carries amino acids to ribosomes during translation


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

mRNA's primary function is to carry genetic information transcribed from DNA to the ribosomes, where it directs protein synthesis.  Pair 1 is correct. tRNA's crucial role is to deliver specific amino acids to the ribosomes during translation, based on the mRNA codons. Pair 4 is incorrect. rRNA constitutes the structural and catalytic core of ribosomes, essential for protein synthesis. Pair 3 is correct. siRNAs are involved in the RNA interference pathway, triggering mRNA degradation or translational repression. Pair 2 is incorrect. Therefore, only pairs 1 and 3 are accurately matched.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Nuclear Reactor Type                     Key Feature
1. Pressurized Heavy Water Reactor (PHWR) : Uses liquid sodium coolant
2. Fast Breeder Reactor (FBR)            :  Breeds more fissile material than consumed
3. Thorium Reactor                         : Primarily uses Uranium-233 as fuel

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only the second pair is correctly matched. Fast Breeder Reactors (FBRs) are indeed designed to breed more fissile material than they consume, a key feature that distinguishes them from other reactor types.  This characteristic is crucial for improving fuel efficiency and reducing reliance on uranium resources.  The other pairs are incorrect. PHWRs utilize heavy water as a moderator and coolant, not liquid sodium, which is a characteristic of some FBR designs.  While thorium reactors utilize thorium, their primary fuel is actually Uranium-233, produced from the thorium.  The use of Uranium-233 is a consequence of thorium's conversion into a fissile material through neutron absorption.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Gene Therapy Application              Specific Disease Treated
1. CRISPR technology                     : Haemophilia A
2. Lentiviral vector                       : Sickle Cell Anemia
3.  FVIII transgene                        : Cystic Fibrosis

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Only the first pair is correctly matched. CRISPR technology, a powerful genome editing tool, is used in gene therapy to correct genetic defects that cause diseases like Haemophilia A.  The other pairs are incorrect. Lentiviral vectors are indeed used as delivery systems in gene therapy, but they are not specifically linked to Sickle Cell Anemia;  multiple vector types are used for various genetic diseases.  Similarly, FVIII transgene is used in gene therapy for Haemophilia A, not Cystic Fibrosis, which involves different genetic mutations and therapeutic approaches.

(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Only the second and third pairs are correctly matched.  The Agni Prime is indeed a short-range ballistic missile, and the Dhanush is a short-range, land-based ballistic missile, not a cruise missile. (d) 1, 2, and 3

Therefore, only the first and third pairs are correctly matched.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Disease                                       Transmission Method
1. COVID-19                                   :   Aerosol droplets
2. Tuberculosis                               :   Airborne droplets
3. HIV/AIDS                                  :   Bodily fluids
4. Cholera                                    :   Contaminated water
5. Malaria                                   :   Mosquito bite


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

COVID-19 primarily spreads through respiratory droplets produced when an infected person coughs or sneezes.  Tuberculosis is also spread through airborne droplets expelled by an infected individual when they cough, sneeze, speak, or sing.  HIV/AIDS, however, is transmitted through direct contact with infected bodily fluids, primarily blood, semen, vaginal fluids, and breast milk. Cholera is a waterborne disease caused by ingesting contaminated water or food. Malaria is a parasitic disease transmitted to humans through the bite of infected female Anopheles mosquitoes.  All the pairs listed are correctly matched based on the established scientific understanding of disease transmission. Options (a), (b), and (c) are therefore incomplete, omitting at least one correctly matched pair.



**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Government Initiative/Program          Focus Area
1. INSPIRE                                 :   Science and Technology Research
2. NTEP                                    :   Tuberculosis Control
3. PMASBY                                  :   COVID-19 Pandemic Response
4. National Vector Borne Disease Control Programme (NVBDCP)  :    Malaria Eradication
