(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

INSPIRE (Innovation in Science Pursuit for Inspired Research) is a flagship program of the Department of Science and Technology, Government of India, aimed at attracting talent to science and research.  NTEP (National Tuberculosis Elimination Programme) is a government initiative dedicated to combating tuberculosis in India. PMASBY (Pradhan Mantri Atma Nirbhar Swasth Bharat Yojana) is a health infrastructure development scheme launched in response to the COVID-19 pandemic.  The National Vector Borne Disease Control Programme (NVBDCP) focuses on controlling vector-borne diseases, including malaria. "The Big Catch-Up" is a program designed to address the learning loss experienced by students due to school closures during the COVID-19 pandemic. All the pairs are correctly matched. Options (a), (b), and (c) are incomplete, failing to include all the correctly matched pairs.



**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Virus                                      Characteristic/Effect
1. Zika Virus                                :   Transmitted by Aedes mosquitoes
2. Ebola Virus                               :   Hemorrhagic fever
3. Nipah Virus                               :   Zoonotic disease (animal to human transmission)
4. Avian Influenza A (H9N2) Virus         :   Bird flu
5. Hepatitis C Virus                         :   Affects the liver


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) Only one
(b) Only two
(c) Only three
(d) All five


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Zika virus is primarily transmitted to people through the bite of an infected Aedes species mosquito. Ebola virus causes a severe hemorrhagic fever, characterized by bleeding, organ failure, and high mortality rates. Nipah virus is a zoonotic virus, meaning it can be transmitted from animals to humans. Avian influenza A (H9N2) virus is a subtype of influenza A virus that can cause both human influenza (though rare) and bird flu. Hepatitis C virus is a viral infection that primarily affects the liver.  All five pairs correctly link the virus to its key characteristic or effect. Therefore, option (d) is the accurate response.

   Concept/Term                                 Description

**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Genetic Factor                     Effect on Progeny

3. Mutations                         : Variation in genetic material

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Sexual reproduction introduces genetic variation in progeny due to the combination of genetic material from two parents. Asexual reproduction generally leads to genetically identical offspring, although mutations can still occur and cause variation. Mutations are a primary source of genetic variation.  Therefore, only pair 3 is correctly matched. Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect because they incorrectly include pairs 1 and/or 2.

**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Type of Memory                     Example
1. Primary Memory                   : Solid State Drive (SSD)
2. Secondary Memory                 : Random Access Memory (RAM)
3. Secondary Memory                 : Hard Disk Drive (HDD)

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Primary memory (RAM) is volatile memory that stores data temporarily while the computer is running. Secondary memory (Hard Disk Drive, SSD, USB) is non-volatile memory that stores data permanently, even when the computer is turned off.  Therefore, only pair 3 is correctly matched. Option (a) and (b) are incorrect as they involve primary memory being wrongly considered as secondary memory. Option (d) is incorrect because it wrongly includes pair 2.

**7. Consider the following pairs:**

   Database Type                    Function
1. Domain Name System (DNS)       : Contains names and addresses of internet hosts

3. Domain Name Service (DNS)      :  Manages internet protocol addresses

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The Domain Name System (DNS) is a hierarchical naming system that translates domain names (e.g., www.example.com) into IP addresses (e.g., 192.168.1.1), making it easier for users to access websites.  While DNS involves various components and processes, the core function of DNS is to provide a mapping between human-readable domain names and machine-readable IP addresses.  The other options describe functions that are either related but not directly the core function of DNS or are inaccurate descriptions. Therefore, only pair 1 is completely accurate.

   Technology                         Description

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?

(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

**5. With reference to Recombinant DNA technology, consider the following pairs:**

   Step                                     Process/Component

**6. Consider the following pairs:**

**7.  Consider the following pairs:**

   Event/Disease              Impact/Consequence
1. Bengal Famine               Malaria outbreak
2. Plague epidemic (14th century)   Significant population decline
3. Loo (local wind)             Increased malaria incidence


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

While the Bengal Famine led to widespread death and suffering, the direct causal link to a *specific* malaria outbreak is not definitively established as the primary cause.  The 14th-century plague epidemic (Black Death) resulted in a massive reduction in the global population. The Loo wind, being hot and dry, actually *reduces* malaria incidence due to its desiccating effect on mosquito breeding grounds.  Therefore, only the second pair is definitively and accurately matched.  This question tests the candidate's ability to evaluate the causal relationships between historical events and their consequences, a skill crucial for the UPSC history and geography sections. The options are designed to challenge the candidate's understanding and prevent simple guessing.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Biotechnological Technique/Tool        Specific Application
1. Recombinant DNA technology           :   Producing human insulin
2. CRISPR-Cas9 gene editing             :   Treating sickle cell anemia
3.  Allogeneic stem cell transplantation :   Treating leukemia


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Recombinant DNA technology is a cornerstone of biotechnology, and its application in producing human insulin is a well-established fact.  The process involves inserting the human insulin gene into a suitable vector (like bacteria), allowing the bacteria to produce large quantities of human insulin, which is then purified for medicinal use.  This has revolutionized the treatment of diabetes.

CRISPR-Cas9 gene editing offers precise gene modification capabilities.  Sickle cell anemia, a genetic disorder caused by a mutation in the hemoglobin gene, is a prime target for CRISPR-based therapies.  Clinical trials have shown promising results in correcting the genetic defect responsible for the disease, offering a potential cure.

Allogeneic stem cell transplantation involves using healthy stem cells from a donor to replace damaged or diseased stem cells in the recipient.  Leukemia, a type of blood cancer, is often treated with this procedure.  The transplanted stem cells can regenerate healthy blood cells, replacing the cancerous ones. The success of these procedures depends on the compatibility between the donor and recipient.  Therefore, all three pairs are correctly matched, showcasing the advancements in biotechnology and medicine.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Chemical Compound/Element       Environmental Impact/Role
1. Nitrate                            :   Component of acid rain
2. Arsenic                           :   Contaminates groundwater
3. Ammonia                           :    Used in fertilizer production


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

While nitrate can contribute to acid rain through atmospheric reactions, its primary environmental impact is related to eutrophication (excessive nutrient enrichment in water bodies) and nitrogen leaching.  The statement in the pair is not entirely incorrect, but it's not the most accurate or prominent effect.  Therefore, it is not a strong match.

Arsenic contamination of groundwater is a significant global environmental problem, particularly in regions like Bangladesh and parts of India.  The presence of arsenic in drinking water poses serious health risks, making this a strong and correct match.

Ammonia is a crucial component of nitrogenous fertilizers.  Its use in agriculture is extensive, and it plays a vital role in boosting crop yields.  Therefore, this is a correct match as well.  Option (c) is the most accurate.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Biological Entity/Process           Characteristic/Function
1. Stem cells                          :    Found only in embryos
2.  Lentiviruses                       :    Used in gene therapy
3.  Gene silencing                     :   Always irreversible


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 only
(d) None

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The statement that stem cells are found *only* in embryos is incorrect. While embryonic stem cells are a significant type, adult stem cells are also present in various tissues throughout the body, capable of self-renewal and differentiation.

Lentiviruses are retroviruses that can integrate their genetic material into the host cell's genome, making them effective vectors for gene therapy.  This makes the pair a correct match.

Gene silencing, a process of regulating gene expression, is often *reversible*.  While some forms can be relatively permanent, epigenetic modifications (like DNA methylation) are often reversible, affecting gene expression without altering the DNA sequence itself.  Thus, this pair is incorrect.  Only pair 2 is correctly matched.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Organization/Initiative             Area of Focus
1. ISRO                                 :   Development of  cryogenic engines
2.  CSIR-CCMB                         :   Epigenetic epidemiology research
3.  ICMR                               :   Development of COVID-19 vaccines


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

ISRO (Indian Space Research Organisation) has a significant program focused on developing and mastering cryogenic engine technology for its launch vehicles.  This is crucial for achieving greater payload capacity and accessing higher orbits.  Therefore, this pair is correctly matched.

CSIR-CCMB (Centre for Cellular and Molecular Biology) is actively involved in research related to epigenetics and its implications for human health and disease.  Their participation in the DEEP project underscores their commitment to this area.  Thus, this is correctly matched.

While ICMR (Indian Council of Medical Research) plays a crucial role in medical research in India, its primary focus isn't vaccine development.  It coordinates and supports various research initiatives, but vaccine development is typically undertaken by other institutions or in collaboration with various organizations.  Therefore, this pair is not correctly matched. Options (a) and (b) are plausible distractors, but only (b) is entirely correct.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

  Genetically Modified Crop         Specific Genetic Modification
1. Bt Cotton                         :   Herbicide tolerance
2.  GM Mustard                       :   Male sterility for hybrid seed production
3.  Bollgard II Bt Cotton              :    Resistance to lepidopteran pests


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Bt cotton is primarily engineered for pest resistance, not herbicide tolerance. Herbicide tolerance is a separate genetic modification often stacked with Bt traits (as seen in HT Bt cotton), but it isn't the defining feature of Bt cotton itself.

GM mustard, specifically the DMH-11 variety, incorporates a barnase-barstar system to induce male sterility in one parent line, facilitating hybrid seed production. This is a key characteristic of this GM crop.

Bollgard II cotton is designed with stacked genes (Cry1Ac and Cry2Ab) to provide broader resistance against a wider range of lepidopteran (moth and butterfly) pests, enhancing its effectiveness compared to earlier generations of Bt cotton. Therefore, only pairs 2 and 3 are correctly matched.  Option (a) is a plausible distractor, but it is incorrect.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Chemical Compound                     Location/Source
1. Cyanide                               :   Northern and Eastern India
2. Sulfuric Acid                           :   Venus's atmosphere
3. Phosphine                               :   Venus's atmosphere
4. Glucosinolates                         :  Indian Mustard (Brassica juncea)

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Cyanide is a byproduct of the coking process and is associated with mustard oil production in Northern and Eastern India, where traditional methods may sometimes lead to contamination.  Sulfuric acid is a major component of Venus's dense atmosphere, contributing to its extreme greenhouse effect.  Phosphine has been detected in Venus's atmosphere, although its origin remains a subject of scientific investigation. Glucosinolates are naturally occurring compounds found in high concentrations in Indian Mustard. Option (a) is incorrect because it only includes cyanide, ignoring the correct pairings of sulfuric acid and phosphine with their respective locations. Option (b) is partially correct regarding cyanide and sulfuric acid but omits the correct pairing of phosphine and its location. Option (c) correctly links sulfuric acid and phosphine to Venus but ignores the correct association of cyanide with mustard oil production regions.  Therefore, only option (d) encompasses all the correctly matched pairs.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Organ                                  Characteristic/Association
1. Liver                                  :   Affected by Hepatitis A
2. Kidney                                 :   Albumin release in urine indicates potential failure
3. Heart                                  :   Located in Afghanistan (Incorrect)
4. Spleen                                 :   Source of donation from living donors (Incorrect)

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Hepatitis A is a viral liver disease, making the first pair correct.  The presence of albumin in urine (albuminuria) is a key indicator of kidney damage or failure, hence the second pair is also correct.  The third and fourth pairs are incorrect.  The heart's geographical location is not specific to Afghanistan; it's a vital organ found in all mammals. While living organ donation is possible, the spleen is not commonly donated from living donors compared to the liver or kidney, making the fourth pair factually wrong. Therefore, only the first two pairs are correctly matched.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Celestial Object/Phenomenon          Characteristic/Property
1. Black Hole                             :   Located in the Milky Way Galaxy
2. Black Hole                             :   Mediated by Gravitational Lensing
3. Venus                                  :   Retrograde Rotation
4. Earth                                   :   Nearest planetary neighbor to Venus

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Black holes are indeed found within the Milky Way Galaxy, confirming the first pair.  Black holes significantly influence gravitational lensing, a phenomenon where light bends around massive objects.  Venus is known for its unique retrograde rotation, spinning in the opposite direction to most other planets. Earth is the closest planet to Venus. All the pairs are correctly matched. Therefore, option (d) is the correct answer.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Spacecraft/Mission                     Target Planet
1. VERITAS                               :   Venus
2. DAVINCI                               :   Venus
3. Mariner 2                             :   Venus
4.  Juno                                  :   Jupiter (Incorrect)

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, and 4


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

VERITAS and DAVINCI are both NASA missions specifically designed to study Venus.  Mariner 2 was a historical mission that also targeted Venus.  The Juno mission, however, focuses on Jupiter.  Therefore, only the first three pairs are correctly matched. Option (d) is incorrect as it includes Juno, which is a mission to Jupiter, not Venus.


**5. Consider the following pairs:**

   Location                                 Significance
1. Kakrapar                              :   Nuclear Power Plant
2. Pokhran                                :   Nuclear Test Site

4. Sriharikota                             :   Satellite Launching Station

Kakrapar is the site of a significant nuclear power plant in India. Pokhran is renowned for its history as a nuclear test site. All four pairs are correctly matched.


**6. Consider the following pairs:**

   Technology/System                     Type of Communication
1. Television Transmission             :   Simplex Communication (Incorrect)
2. Email                                :   Full-duplex Communication (Incorrect)
3. Internet                              :  Network of Networks
4.  Extranet                             : Network of Networks (Incorrect)


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 3 and 4 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Television transmission is not simplex (one-way) communication; it's a more complex system. Email typically allows for two-way communication but not simultaneously. The Internet is fundamentally a network of networks.  Extranet is a type of network, but not a network of networks in the same sense as the Internet. Therefore, only the statement about the Internet is correctly matched.


**7. Consider the following pairs:**

   Causative Agent                         Disease/Condition
1. E. coli                                 :   Food Poisoning
2. Salmonella bacilli                     :   Food Poisoning
3. Pseudomonas                           :   Food Poisoning
4. Candida                               :   Food Poisoning (Incorrect)


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3 and 4


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

*E. coli*, *Salmonella bacilli*, and *Pseudomonas* are all bacteria known to cause food poisoning under certain conditions.  Candida, however, is a type of yeast and is more commonly associated with fungal infections rather than food poisoning.  Therefore, only the first three pairs are correctly matched.


**8. Consider the following pairs:**

   Medical Term/Concept                  Description/Association
1. AIDS                                  :   Immune system affected
2. T-lymphocytes                         :   Completely damaged in AIDS
3.  Hepatitis A                           :   Affects the Liver
4. Albuminuria                           : Indicates Kidney Failure


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, 3 and 4


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

AIDS severely compromises the immune system.  T-lymphocytes are crucial immune cells that are significantly depleted in AIDS. Hepatitis A primarily affects the liver. Albuminuria (albumin in the urine) is a sign of kidney dysfunction.  All four pairs are correctly matched.

**1. Consider the following pairs:**

   Immune Cell Type                    Primary Function
1. B Lymphocytes                     :     Kill virally infected cells
2. Cytotoxic T cells                  :     Produce antibodies
3. Natural Killer (NK) cells          :     Mediate cellular immunity
4. Helper T cells                      :     Regulate immune response
5. Regulatory T cells                 :     Assist in B cell activation

Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 4 and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Option (d) is correct because Helper T cells (Th) are crucial in assisting the activation of B cells and cytotoxic T cells, initiating and coordinating the adaptive immune response.  Regulatory T cells (Treg) play a vital role in maintaining immune homeostasis by suppressing excessive immune responses and preventing autoimmunity.  These are their primary functions.  The other options are incorrect. B lymphocytes primarily produce antibodies, not directly kill infected cells. That is the function of cytotoxic T cells. Natural Killer cells, indeed, are part of the innate immune system and kill infected or cancerous cells without prior sensitization; they do not mediate cellular immunity in the same way as T cells. Therefore, only the pairing of Helper T cells with their assisting role and Regulatory T cells with their regulatory function are accurately matched.  The question tests factual recall of the basic functions of different immune cells, a crucial concept in immunology and frequently relevant in UPSC examinations relating to diseases and their treatments.


**2. Consider the following pairs:**

   Immunity Type                       Characteristic
1. Innate Immunity                   :     Develops after antigen exposure
2. Adaptive Immunity                 :     First line of defense
3. Passive Immunity                   :     Acquired through antibody transfer
4. Active Immunity                    :     Long-lasting, specific response
5. Natural Immunity                   :     Stimulated by vaccination


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 4 and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Option (c) is correct. Passive immunity is indeed acquired through the transfer of antibodies or activated T cells from an immune host, such as from mother to fetus. Active immunity is characterized by a long-lasting, specific response developed after exposure to an antigen, whether through infection or vaccination. The other options are incorrect because innate immunity is the body's first line of defense, not adaptive immunity.  Adaptive immunity develops after exposure to antigens, not innate immunity. Natural immunity is acquired through natural processes like infection, not vaccination which is a form of artificial immunity.  This question tests the understanding of different types of immunity and their mechanisms, a fundamental concept in immunology regularly assessed in the UPSC examination.


**3. Consider the following pairs:**

   Immune Response                    Description
1. Humoral Immunity                 :     Mediated by T cells
2. Cellular Immunity                 :     Involves antibody production
3. Immunological Memory              :     Rapid, effective response to re-infection
4. Autoimmunity                     :     Immune response against self-antigens
5. Allergy                           :     Hypersensitivity to environmental antigens


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 and 4 only
(d) 4 and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Option (d) is correct. Autoimmunity is correctly defined as an immune response directed against the body's own tissues and cells.  Allergy is accurately described as a hypersensitivity reaction to environmental antigens. The other options are incorrect. Humoral immunity is mediated by antibodies produced by B cells, not T cells. Cellular immunity is primarily mediated by T cells, not antibodies. Immunological memory is the ability of the immune system to mount a faster and stronger response upon secondary exposure to a pathogen, which is true but not the primary definition. This question assesses the understanding of different immune responses and disorders, a crucial topic for the UPSC examination.  The distractors involve switching the definitions of humoral and cellular immunity, a common area of confusion for candidates.


**4. Consider the following pairs:**

   Vaccine Type                      Mechanism of Action
1. mRNA Vaccine                     :     Uses weakened or killed pathogens
2. Conventional Vaccine             :     Introduces mRNA to produce viral proteins
3. DNA Vaccine                       :     Introduces plasmid DNA to produce viral proteins
4. Hepatitis A Vaccine              :     Provides lifelong immunity against infection
5. Hepatitis C Vaccine              :     Currently unavailable


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 and 5 only
(d) 4 and 5 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Option (c) is the correct answer. A DNA vaccine correctly uses plasmid DNA to produce viral proteins within the body's cells to trigger an immune response.  There is currently no licensed vaccine for Hepatitis C, making this statement true.  The other options are incorrect. mRNA vaccines do not use weakened or killed pathogens; they use mRNA to instruct cells to produce viral proteins.  Conventional vaccines typically use weakened or killed pathogens or their components.  While some vaccines provide long-lasting immunity, it is not necessarily lifelong for all vaccines, including the Hepatitis A vaccine. This question tests the knowledge of different vaccine types and their mechanisms, a very important topic for the UPSC given the increasing relevance of vaccines in public health. The distractors focus on common misconceptions regarding vaccine mechanisms and long-term efficacy.


**5.  Consider the following pairs:**

   Disease                                      Causative Agent
1. AIDS                                         :     Virus
2. Tuberculosis (TB)                             :     Bacteria
3. Lymphatic Filariasis (Elephantiasis)      :     Nematode worms
4. Malaria                                      :     Protozoa
5. Hepatitis C                                   :     Fungus


Which of the pairs given above is/are correctly matched?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, 3, and 4 only
(d) 1, 2, 3, 4, and 5


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Option (c) correctly matches AIDS with a virus (HIV), Tuberculosis with bacteria (Mycobacterium tuberculosis), and Lymphatic Filariasis with nematode worms (filarial worms). Malaria is caused by Plasmodium protozoa.  The pairing of Hepatitis C with a fungus is incorrect; Hepatitis C is caused by a virus (Hepatitis C virus).  This question tests factual recall of the causative agents of several important diseases, a frequently examined area in the UPSC syllabus.  The distractors involve substituting the correct causative agents with closely related ones, or introducing a completely unrelated one (fungus in the case of Hepatitis C). The ability to correctly identify the causative agents is key to understanding disease transmission, prevention, and treatment strategies.
